Shen Bao Medicine and Pharmacy Weekly

An Overview of Medicine and Pharmacy in Shanghai in the Past Decade (Continued) 160

— Pang Jingzhou

What Shanghai feels particularly lacking and urgently needs to promote is infectious disease hospitals. According to the current situation, there are only a few hospitals that specialize in treating dangerous infectious diseases, such as meningitis, scarlet fever, and smallpox. The Public Concession's Public Works Department has an isolation hospital, but the Chinese department inside is really not praised by the Chinese. Therefore, patients are terrified when they hear that they are going to the Public Works Department Hospital. The French Concession's Guangci Hospital has a separate Chenli Hospital Department. However, the system is very biased and isolated from other medical circles. And it is not very convenient to only accept residents of the French Concession. The Shanghai Municipal Shanghai Hospital in Nanshi also has considerable isolation beds during the epidemic period of the above-mentioned diseases, but the houses there are too unsuitable. Collecting too many dangerous cases will hinder other wards. There used to be a public hospital in Zhabei, which was run by the Chinese. It specialized in receiving such symptoms. The location and architecture were very good, and the qualifications were the oldest, but the medical affairs were completely contracted by a foreigner, which was somewhat inconsistent with the new academic theory. For example, scarlet fever does not allow much blood serum to be injected, and the throat is smeared with medicine every day, which often makes the patient sit up, regardless of the danger of the heart. These are all I have witnessed with my own eyes. Now, after the war in Zhabei, the hospital has also been hit. In addition, the Red Cross Society has been intermittent in the operation of isolation hospitals, and the Health Bureau has no funds to open them, so開業physicians are most hesitant when diagnosing such diseases, persuading patients to send them to the above-mentioned hospitals. They are mostly unwilling. If they are sent to other wards, they will be rejected. Listen to them being treated at home. It is greatly inconsistent with the principles of public health, and especially violates the responsibilities of a proper doctor. Therefore, enthusiastic doctors, regardless of whether the patient is willing or not, report to the Public Works Department and forcibly take the patient away. Slightly passive doctors follow the patient's requirements and take a great risk to treat him at home with the business experience of daily visits. The most passive doctors completely abandon this patient, let him eat immortal prescriptions or soup heads, and ignore whether he infects others. The so-called major infectious diseases in Shanghai are also流行流行 under this畸形 medicine, rising and falling with the weather. The Public Works Department actually publishes a report in the newspaper every week, saying that there are so many cases of smallpox and so many cases of scarlet fever. Where is the auditable exact number? It can be said that all those who eat immortal prescriptions, invite otolaryngologists, and apply plasters are completely not included. It is not easy to investigate even deaths. However, assuming that all cases are sent to isolation hospitals in accordance with legal procedures, I am afraid that the above-mentioned hospitals will be overcrowded. This situation should be worthy of attention by thoughtful people in society.

Next, let’s talk about cholera hospitals, commonly known as epidemic hospitals, which are popular in summer. Most of the cholera patients are civilians and laborers, so the way of running such hospitals is often like giving free clinics, in a charitable way. However, cholera is not limited to civilians, and middle-class merchants, high officials and wealthy businessmen also suffer from cholera if they are not careful in their diet, so the difficulty of hospitalization arises. If you say that高等sanatoriums or private hospitals accept cholera, it is actually somewhat illegal. If you say that you live in the same room with peddlers and pawnbrokers, it is also something that the upper class people do not want. Although there are several epidemic hospitals with first- and second-class chargeable rooms, unfortunately they are temporary and things are very chaotic, and the first- and second-class are not well-studied. There are patients who say to the people in the epidemic hospital: "I would rather pay more hospital fees, please treat and care for me more authentically." However, everyone in the hospital can only reply: "There are many people and things here, so we have to treat everyone equally." In your self-governing epidemic hospital, especially the completely free clinic nature, we cannot accept half a cent no matter how much he is willing to pay, and there is really nothing authentic about nursing supplies. Therefore, I think that in Shanghai, during the annual cholera epidemic, it may be appropriate to adapt to the actual needs and organize one or two more advanced epidemic hospitals, with complete disinfection equipment, proper nursing medicine, and higher charges. There is no need for too many beds, only for the use of the property-owning class who occasionally suffer from cholera (that is, dysentery can also be accepted and retained), so as to avoid the other ordinary hospitals being disturbed by those infectious patients, and to avoid many patients filling the family alleys with infectious excrement because they are afraid of entering ordinary epidemic hospitals.

Talking About Hemoptysis 161

— Liang Junqing

Hemoptysis is a symptom, not a disease. Generally speaking, people think that hemoptysis is tuberculosis (meaning pulmonary tuberculosis). In fact, there are many causes of hemoptysis. Tuberculosis is just one of the causes. Even in terms of the blood that is coughed up, some comes from the lungs, some comes directly from the heart, some comes from the stomach, and some comes from the throat, nasal cavity, and oral cavity. All must be distinguished and diagnosed, and cannot be confused. Moreover, the blood that comes from the lungs is not necessarily caused by tuberculosis. For example, if the lungs have syphilis, hemoptysis can occur. If the pulmonary trachea expands and ruptures, hemoptysis can occur. If the pulmonary blood vessels are blocked by blood clots (the main cause is heart disease), hemoptysis can also occur. If the lungs suffer from actinomycosis or carbuncle, hemoptysis can occur. If the lungs suffer from cysticercosis or Paragonimus disease (also known as lung fluke, the symptoms of which are very similar to tuberculosis), there is even the possibility of hemoptysis. If a woman has retrograde menstruation, or if the aortic aneurysm ruptures into the pulmonary trachea, the blood can also be coughed up from the pulmonary trachea. I remember that a certain patient suddenly coughed up blood. The doctor diagnosed it as tuberculosis and even took an X-ray photograph as proof. Later, after repeated treatment, it was not cured. After careful diagnosis, it was found to be heart disease. The X-ray photograph of a patient with heart disease can sometimes be very similar to tuberculosis and other diseases. As for the blood coughed up from the stomach, it is not all caused by stomach diseases. For example, if the liver is atrophied, the blood will be blocked in the lower part of the esophagus and the stomach. If there is an opportunity, bleeding can occur. The blood gushes up and is hemoptysis. The blood vessels of old people are easily hardened. After the blood vessels of the stomach are hardened, it is also very easy to bleed. The blood accumulates in the stomach mostly and is coughed up. Also, people with typhoid fever or appendicitis sometimes also cough up blood. Other causes such as blood vessel embolism in the intestine, malignant lymphoma, or jaundice can also be the cause of hemoptysis. As for the nose, oral cavity, throat, etc., sometimes due to various reasons, bleeding can occur due to wounds. Those who do not know think it is bleeding from the lungs or stomach. I remember when I was in Germany, I saw a woman suffering from a nervous disorder who came to the lung department seeking treatment for hemoptysis. After repeated examinations, it was not known where the blood came from. However, the sputum bowl on the table was filled with blood every morning. Later, after a secret investigation by the night shift nurse, it was found that the blood she coughed up was caused by her specially piercing her gums with a hair needle. All of this is endless. If it is said that hemoptysis is tuberculosis, wouldn't it be angry? Therefore, if a doctor encounters a patient coughing up blood, if there is any doubt, he must carefully diagnose and distinguish the cause of the disease, and prescribe the right medicine, then it will be effective. And if a patient suffers from hemoptysis, there is no need to panic too much. Don't think that it is tuberculosis and be disheartened. It is best to ask the doctor to carefully diagnose. As for the method of differentiating and diagnosing hemoptysis, it is quite complicated. Sometimes X-ray examination is required, sometimes microscopic examination is required, sometimes serum examination is required, and sometimes chemical examination is required. There are many kinds. I will not list them all. If I have time in the future, I will write a detailed explanation. However, regarding the above-mentioned examination, it is best to be able to implement it yourself. Sometimes, when encountering critically ill patients who must be examined, it is impossible to delay the time.

Since the causes of hemoptysis are as complicated as described above, the main treatment drugs also vary with the disease, and cannot be confined to one prescription. (End)

A Humble Opinion on Preventing Meningitis 162

— Wang Yaobai

(I) The Course of the Epidemic

Meningitis was formerly only an occasional epidemic. Since the European War, it has transformed into a large-scale epidemic. According to the records of the Journal of the American Medical Association, the great epidemic of this disease began after the European War. It was first discovered in Austria in 1917, and then spread from west to east, from France to England. In 1919, it reached the Americas. In the spring of 1920, Shanghai newspapers reported that the disease was found in Shanghai, thus it crossed the Pacific Ocean and reached China. Subsequently, it spread from Shanghai along the railway lines to various parts of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. This can be traced on a map. In March of that year, I was in Changzhou. When it was first discovered, I translated and published the articles from the American Medical Journal in various newspapers for colleagues to study and verify. Since then, between the winter and spring of each year, there has been an epidemic of this disease. In recent years, it has been particularly prevalent, with Jiangnan and western Zhejiang being the main areas of occurrence. This is probably due to the convenience of transportation and the rapid dissemination of information, hence the increased awareness.

(II) Variations in Symptoms

The common symptoms of this disease are fever, headache, vomiting, and gradually stiff neck muscles, leading to opisthotonos. However, there are also many exceptional and unusual symptoms that are easily mistaken. For example, when this disease was first seen in rural Huzhou, patients only complained of slight headaches, without fever or convulsions. Examination of their cerebrospinal fluid showed it to be very clear. However, shortly afterwards, purple spots appeared all over their bodies. A further examination of the cerebrospinal fluid revealed a large number of bacteria. From the onset of the disease to death, it took only a dozen hours. Also, there was a child in Hangzhou, only eight months old, whose fontanelle was swollen. The family suspected it was a seasonal illness and requested an examination of the cerebrospinal fluid. No bacteria were found, but the child became seriously ill and died. The family agreed to a post-mortem examination to find out what happened. The results showed that the meninges were indeed inflamed. Meningitis, as seen in Jiaxing, initially presented with vomiting and diarrhea, very similar to cholera, but bacteria could be detected in the cerebrospinal fluid. Therefore, doctors and patients should be aware of this when encountering suspicious symptoms.

(III) Opinions on Prevention and Treatment

(A) There are various preventive methods. However, the most effective is the injection of meningitis vaccine. However, it must be administered early, before the epidemic occurs. Each vaccination needs to be done every week for three weeks to give a full immune response. Thus, it is advisable to promote vaccination in winter or early spring to prevent problems before they arise. If you have already been in contact with a patient, then serum should be used as a preventative injection. The Huzhou Health Association vaccinated more than 4,000 people in urban and rural areas with the preventative vaccine and none of them were infected. In a certain hospital, more than a hundred employees were given preventative injections. Unexpectedly, three nurses later contracted the disease. Upon investigation, it was found that they had not received preventative injections due to some reason. This is a very powerful counter-proof. The epidemic was particularly severe in Changzhou last year. A temporary preventative vaccination program was initiated, and it was later divided into two areas, north and south. I was in charge of the Gospel Hospital in the northern district. A total of more than 3,000 people were vaccinated and none of those vaccinated were subsequently infected. (B) Treatment - Meningitis serum is, of course, the only specific drug for this disease. What should be noted is that the earlier it is used, the better. When the disease is prevalent, meningitis serum can be used for intramuscular injection when similar illnesses are encountered, often taking the initiative and eliminating the disease before it takes hold. If one must wait until bacteria are found in the spinal fluid examination before using it, it often leads to mistakes. This is because there are often cases where the initial examination shows no bacteria. The patient deteriorates after a few hours. A second spinal fluid examination shows there are many bacteria. Treatment may then be too late. Also, if spinal fluid injections alone are not very effective, intravenous injections can be used in conjunction with them, which may be more beneficial.

(IV) Origin of Serum

Regarding the origin of serum and vaccines, there is an important fact that should be brought to the special attention of Chinese people. The common view is that imported goods are more exquisite and superior to domestically produced goods. However, in the case of serum or vaccines for treating infectious diseases, the opposite is true. According to the results of experiments in various mission hospitals, domestically produced serum and vaccines are actually far more effective than imported goods. Some initially thought that this was simply because the products were fresher. However, according to Dr. Xi Youkang's opinion, it is due to the types of bacteria. It was also discovered that in the European War. Soldiers came from all over the world. Serum and other medicines were also collected and concentrated from various places and distributed for use. Unexpectedly, when serum from country A was used to treat patients from country B, the effect was greatly reduced. After repeated research, it was realized that if the bacterial strains used to manufacture the serum were taken from people of the same region, the types would be more similar, and the attacking effect would be greater. I obtained this discovery while collecting treatment results for meningitis. I must report this to the Chinese people. I also hope that domestic institutions that manufacture serum and vaccines will continue to improve the quality of their products to meet the needs of the Chinese people.

Talking about Medicines Brings to Mind National Calamities 163

— Yugong

The Japanese pirates are invading more and more. The nation's lifeline is hanging by a thread. Tracing the origin of the disaster, it is none other than the unequal treaties that have led to this. Because of the unequal treaties, the Japanese are able to openly deploy troops and generals within our country, seeking opportunities to start trouble and create the Mukden Incident, the Shanghai War, and the Battle of Shanhaiguan. Now, a large army is pressing down on our borders, invading Rehe, destroying our defenses, and peeking into our heartland. They all rely on the unequal treaties as a protective talisman. The unequal treaties are the prelude to our country's demise. And the signing of various unequal treaties originated from the Opium War in the 20th year of Daoguang (1840). The opium problem is a matter of life and death for our country and must be described. Opium in England is also known as Opium, which is the most useful medicine and also the most harmful medicine. The word Opium comes from the Greek word Ｏpion, meaning juice. In those days, the juice of plants that could be used for medicinal purposes was called Opion. Later, because poppy flower juice was more effective than the juice of other plants, Opion specifically referred to poppy flower juice. When the world's people learned of the medicinal value of poppy flower juice, very few people knew. The founder of Western medicine, Hippocrates (460-372 BC), knew that its leaves could be used for food, but did not know its medicinal effect. The first person to discover its hypnotic use was Tarentun (240 BC). In the first century, Dioscorides began to make clear records of the medicinal efficacy of opium and the method of collecting opium. However, the reputation of opium was not very prominent at the time. Some people even held opposing views. The most famous pharmacist, Galen, still regarded opium as an extremely dangerous substance and should not be used lightly. As a result, the efficacy of opium was buried for thousands of years. It was not until Felix Platter came out in 1536-1614 that he broke the prejudice and promoted its efficacy. In 1669, the British physician Sydenham made opium into wine, which is still used today. However, the person who made a great contribution to opium was Serturoer in 1815, who proposed the alkali. This alkali is named Morpheum to commemorate the god of dreams, Morpheus. The method of collecting opium is to make a number of scratches on the outer skin of the fruit with a knife at night when the dew is down. The depth of the scratches is very important. If the scratches are too deep, the opium juice may be lost. Within 24 hours, the collector must go to the field to carefully scrape off the flowing juice and place it in a plate. Then, the dried juice is packed into round blocks. This is the opium sold on the market. The first time opium came to China was in the ninth century. At that time, a Western doctor named Moors used it to treat dysentery and it was quite effective. At the end of the 17th century, Chinese people began to smoke it. Who started it is unknown. According to rumors, it was either the Persians or the Turks. They initially mixed opium with tobacco leaves and smoked it. The method was spread to China, where the Chinese made special equipment and used a pipe to pick and smoke it. Then, they only smoked opium and did not mix it with tobacco leaves. The initial amount of opium imported into China was very small. In 1787, the British East India Company established an opium depot near Hong Kong, which greatly increased the transportation of opium. The number of smokers increased day by day. Chinese people became addicted to smoking, which led to weakness and waste. The Chinese government had no choice but to take strict measures. In 1796, it issued an edict prohibiting smoking. In 1820, it prohibited opium ships from entering Guangzhou, which led to the Opium War in 1840. As a result, China was defeated miserably. In 1842, the Treaty of Nanjing was concluded, opening five ports for trade. From then on, the transportation of opium to China was no longer a prohibited item. Since then, various unequal treaties have continued to be signed. The powers have used various unequal treaties as tools to invade China. The cause of today's national crisis is the unequal treaties. The cause of the unequal treaties is opium. Opium, opium, you are really the vanguard of imperialism.

Common Sense Questions and Answers about Diseases (Continued) 164

— Cheng Hanzhang

Q: Is measles prevention dangerous to life?

A: Not dangerous. The mortality rate is roughly 3%. It can be seen that infants and children with weak constitutions are relatively more at risk.

Q: What is the general treatment for measles?

A: Keep the sickroom warm, humid, dim, and quiet for rest. Apply an ice pack to the head and a warm, moist cloth to the chest. Sometimes apply mustard.

Q: How should one deal with various symptoms?

A: When there is a fever, use a sweating method. Drink hot beverages, and occasionally use euquinine. When coughing, use inhalation, gargling, or take expectorant and cough suppressant. For itchy skin during the rash, use sterile oil and cloth. Wash the eyes with boric acid water and apply boric acid ointment to the nose or drop in Mistol.

Q: How should one take care of oneself after recovering from measles?

A: Wait one week after the fever has completely subsided before getting out of bed. You can go out after another week. During the recovery period, do not catch a cold to prevent pneumonia and other symptoms.

Q: What methods can be used to prevent measles?

A: Do not get close to people who are already sick (isolation). Injecting serum from patients in the recovery period is a very effective prevention method.

The Social Mission of Doctors (III) 165

— Fan Shouyuan

Although, we want to enable the ordinary public to understand medicine. But of course that is impossible. Not to mention the ordinary public, even the intellectual community, even the people in our own medical field, is impossible. The knowledge we research is only a very small part of what is currently recognized by the scientific community. There are still many, many unknown things in medicine. It can be said that unknown medicine is like a vast ocean. That vast amount of unknown medicine is still waiting for our medical community to study and work hard in the future to discover and explore. The medical knowledge we want to promote is extremely easy and simple, ubiquitous, universally practical, and available at all times. The reason why we have the inescapable responsibility to take on this task of popularization is precisely because the general public lacks this simple and vital everyday knowledge, is too far away from it, pays too little attention to it, and is too ignorant of its value! Therefore, in all aspects of Chinese society, there is a feeling of urgent need for the dissemination of medical knowledge. Shouldn't we doctors respond to the needs of the real world and take on this serious task of benefiting the masses and helping the world?

The above has broadly covered the tasks of doctors to treat the sick and suffering masses, and to publicize medical knowledge; now let us talk about another working task that has the same importance as the above one, that working task is the revolutionary task of anti-unscientific medicine. The so-called unscientific medicine is what people generally call "old medicine", that is. I think the name "old medicine" is very appropriate and fair. However, people in the general old medical community will certainly deny it; even the general public outside the world may inevitably say that it is a kind of sarcastic title of our new medical community for the old doctors. In fact, this is wrong: the so-called old medicine is because it is a kind of metaphysical medical skill of the past era; all its theories are based on the ancient metaphysical medical arguments and doctrines, and they are all restorationists who respect the ancients, copy the ancients, and drive backwards. Why do our scientific new doctors do this opposition work? This is very clear, because modern medicine is an applied science that is part of natural science, it is something that relieves human suffering and protects human health. This has been mentioned above. Since it is an applied science that is applied to the human body, needless to say, we must have a careful observation and accurate research on the organizational structure, physiological state, etc. of the human body in advance. Modern scientific new medicine is based on a kind of knowledge of the human body obtained through a long period of strict observation, accurate field experiments, and field research. The pathology, pharmacology, etc. that start from this kind of scientific foundation are reliable, and they are the true medicine that is not wrong in human health. Old doctors in the early past era also used to put in a lot of effort and hard work to observe and study. At that time, they also had their moment of glory; everyone also regarded him as the central theory at that time. However, the ancient people's observations and ancient people's research were of course not like the methods of applied science now. Therefore, although he observed, he did not observe meticulously; although he researched, he did not research accurately. Therefore, all his theories, all his facts, look irrational, false, and speculative from the perspective of modern science, and they are all groups saying lies.

A Visit to the Xin Ya Chemical Pharmaceutical Factory (Part 2) 166

— Dai Zhi

Working Conditions: Visiting the work inside the Xin Ya Pharmaceutical Factory, first entering the glass department, this department has two large melting furnaces, a rough work and a fine work department, with approximately 100 workers. Every day, it can produce more than 1,000 various sizes of measuring cups, 200 pounds of watch glass raw materials, 500 pounds of various sizes of glass tubes, and the fine work department can produce more than 50,000 ampoules. Next entering the pharmaceutical department, the first room is the tube washing room, which uses tap water pressure to wash, and then distilled water to wash. The second room is the distillation room, then entering is the empty tube drying and sterilization room, with fifty sterilizing dryers. The next is the steam sterilization room. The middle part is the packaging room, employing approximately 100 female workers. The pharmaceutical department has approximately 100 workers. The rear part is the inspection room, where all kinds of sterilized medicines must be inspected before they can be packaged. The precision of its manufacture is evident. As for the pharmaceutical rooms, there are pill rolling machines, mixing machines, mixers, leaching machines, and other refined crystal glass equipment, all self-made by the factory's glass department. Under construction are vacuum reflux machines, vacuum drying machines, electric drying machines, dry distillation machines, evaporators, etc., all extremely complete. The injection liquid filling room, the drug mixing room, and even the research room, the animal testing room, and the bacteria inspection room have all equipment that is especially comprehensive, and the line markings and scales of the measuring cups are all automatically installed, and manufactured according to the Chinese Ministry's standard temperature. Its precision and accuracy can rival imported goods.

Drug Production Conditions: The Xin Ya Pharmaceutical Factory, as described above, is the leading new drug manufacturing factory in the country. Its output is approximately more than 3,000 pieces per day, with a wide variety of items. This reporter is not a pharmacist, so I cannot remember all the product names. Common new drugs, such as sterile distilled water, physiological saline, glucose, calcium chloride, calcium iodide, camphor oil, emetine, quinine injection, etc., total more than 100 kinds. Among the famous ones, such as Fubailong, Kangfuna Xin, Vitamin B, and Vitamin A, can take the place of foreign goods. And Tong Biling (pain reliever), Yisuxiu Mian (sleeping pill), Dainengkeline (yellow pigment injection), Adu Na Xin (hemostatic and cardiotonic), Kang's Syphilis Turbidity Reaction Liquid (toxicity reaction liquid), Liao Saitong (laxative), Glycerin Suppository (suppository), and He Cishi Baoming (tonic) can all seize a part of the position of imported goods, especially those made purely from domestic raw materials, such as Baikeding, (cough suppressant) Angelica Preparations, (angelica preparations) Vitamin B, (ie bran essence) Pizhile, (bran oil) Sanfu Ointment (swelling relieving ointment made with Gaolin soil), etc. In the future, there will be more inventions, and the future is bright, and it is truly unlimited.

The Russian Ukrainian Historical Literature Museum Established 167

Collecting the works of famous artists in abundance

(TASS News Agency, Kakov) At the end of 1932, a Ukrainian Historical Literature Museum was established here. The founders are well-known domestic scientists, writers, and political leaders. The first impression of visitors is the unprecedented development of literature in the past fifteen years. In the old Russian era, only 2,560 kinds of books were published in Ukraine in 120 years, while 6,000 kinds of books were published between 1929 and 1930. The museum also shows evidence that the creation of aesthetic value must be based on social conditions. From this, it can be seen that the economy and politics of a country are closely related. The museum has a large hall with the works of about 100 famous modern writers on display. Each writer has a special shelf, and the writer's political "face" and artistic "face" are revealed here. Another hall is dedicated to displaying the works of foreign writers living in Ukraine. There are 35 writers in total, with texts in Bulgarian, Molu Taiwan, Greek, Armenian Tartar, Polish, German, and Jewish. In addition, translated works also occupy a separate room. Ancient literature from Sophocles to Euripides, Dante, and even Goethe has been translated and completed in recent years.

Ministry Order for Rectifying the Two Law Schools 173

News of the Ministry of Education's rectification of the private Shanghai Law and Political Science College and Shanghai Law College was reported in yesterday's newspaper. The instruction to the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau is recorded below. According to the report of the inspector of this Ministry, the situation of the private Shanghai Law and Political Science College and the private Shanghai Law College is excerpted as follows: Student level: After checking the admission qualifications, many are not in compliance with the regulations. Admission and transfer certificates from the Ministry are also mostly forged. Furthermore, checking the semesters and entrance examination papers reveals that the examination is extremely easy, and the grading is too lenient. The level of Chinese and foreign languages is particularly low. Teacher salaries: The highest monthly salary for full-time teachers is only one hundred and sixty or seventy yuan, and the lowest is thirty or forty yuan. Part-time teachers receive two, three, or four yuan per hour, varying. Curriculum: There are many types of courses, and the order of arrangement is not well considered. Basic courses are mostly lacking. Course materials focus on lectures, with little practical exercise or research. Equipment: The books in the Law and Political Science College library are old and mostly unusable. The Law College library was destroyed in the Shanghai Incident and cannot be verified. What exists now is only newspapers and magazines. Sports fields are lacking in both. Funding: The regular expenses are far from the minimum standard set by the Ministry, and they rely entirely on miscellaneous fee income. Although the Law and Political Science College claims that its funds are deposited in the bank, the college's budget does not list interest income. The Law College's funds have already been used for the construction of school buildings and auditoriums. School buildings: The Law and Political Science College has not fully resolved its debt disputes regarding school buildings. The Law College's school buildings were completely destroyed in the Shanghai Incident and are currently temporarily rented. During classes at the Law and Political Science College, many students at all levels are absent, the order is chaotic, and the spirit is poor. The interior of the school is filthy. The president does not often come to the school, and some teachers and staff receive salaries but do not come to the school to teach or work. In general, the management of these two colleges is very poor and violates many laws and regulations. According to Article 6 of the Regulations for Private Schools and the clear orders from the Central Government to eliminate departments such as literature and law, this Ministry should strictly ban them. However, the colleges are given a final opportunity for improvement and are temporarily handled leniently. They must immediately and rigorously improve. This Ministry will send personnel to inspect again to observe the subsequent effects. This order is to be issued to the Bureau to inform them to comply with it. This order.

Chiao Tung University Purchases Civilian Land to Expand School Site 174

Ministry of Railways Instructs the University to Handle According to Law

Due to the previous purchase of civilian land being insufficient for expansion, National Chiao Tung University intends to continue to collect land to the north and southwest of the school. It specially drafted a plan for purchasing civilian land, including maps and lists, and submitted them to the Ministry of Railways to inform the Ministry of Interior for approval and announcement. Now it has been learned that the Ministry of Interior has replied. The university has also recently received instructions from the Ministry of Railways, stating that the reply has been approved, and it complies with the provisions of the first half of Clause 7 of Article 2 of the Land Expropriation Law. In addition to approving the announcement according to law, two copies of the announcement and a copy of the previously submitted plan are enclosed for review and shall be posted at the expropriation site to inform the public. Still hope to handle according to law, etc., and enclosed the announcement and other documents to the Ministry. According to Article 12 of the Land Expropriation Law, "After the approval by the approving authority in Clause 8, if it is a national or provincial undertaking, the competent authority of the undertaking shall notify the local administrative authority to announce the detailed list of land to be expropriated, and notify the land owners and related parties," etc. In addition to consulting the Shanghai Special Municipal Government for verification and handling, this document is enclosed with Zhang, ordering the school to immediately post them at the expropriation site to inform the public, and also prepare a plan for purchasing civilian land, maps, and a list of the number of acres of civilian land purchased and the names of the owners, and directly contact the Municipal Government to handle it according to law, etc.

Jinan Alumni Association Cables Government to Postpone Increasing Overseas Postage to Nanyang 175

Recently, news reported that the Ministry of Communications had a proposal to increase postage to Nanyang, causing widespread panic. The Shanghai Jinan Alumni Association has always been extremely concerned about overseas Chinese affairs. In order to reduce the burden on overseas Chinese compatriots, it specially cabled the Ministry of Communications to postpone the increase in postage to Nanyang. The text of the cable is recorded below: To Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Communications: Recently, I heard that the Postal Administration is discussing increasing postage to Nanyang. In recent years, overseas Chinese compatriots in Nanyang have suffered from the impact of the world's economic recession, and all industries are declining, making life difficult. Now, the motherland government not only does not provide assistance, but also intends to increase postage to Nanyang, which is contrary to the original intention of caring for overseas Chinese compatriots. Moreover, overseas Chinese compatriots in Nanyang can still enthusiastically donate funds to save the country despite all kinds of difficulties, but our government does not remember this and should not take this kind of measure, which really disappoints overseas Chinese compatriots. Our association is aware of the suffering of overseas Chinese compatriots and dare not remain silent. I specially cable your ministry to quickly order the General Administration of Posts to postpone the increase in postage to Nanyang in order to relieve the difficulties of overseas Chinese. The cable is urgent and awaits your decision. Respectfully, Shanghai Alumni Association of National Jinan University.

Improvement of Chinese Education Publication 181

Several members of the Education Investigation Team of the International Federation, including Mr. Burke, came to China to investigate education under the mandate of the International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation. Their footsteps have traveled north to Beiping and south to Guangzhou. They have seen hundreds of public and private schools of all sizes. The report they have written has been translated into Chinese by the National Bureau of Compilation and Translation, totaling more than 120,000 words. Among them, they pay close attention to the history of modern Chinese education, social conditions, national status, political organization, and even national character, and use it as the basis for all observations and judgments. There are more insightful analyses of the system and policies of education at all levels, as well as its content. The suggestions they make are particularly sincere and are truly a great achievement. The book has arrived in Shanghai and is exclusively sold by the Modern Bookstore on Sima Road, priced at 8 jiao per volume. All schools and libraries can get a 10% discount when purchasing with a seal.

Western League A Group Soccer Match

Performance Reduced, Donghua Ties French Business Association 3-3 186

—After a 3-1 Victory, French Business Association Scores Two Goals in a Row—

The Donghua soccer team, which has won repeatedly, has had smooth sailing in the Western League A group, creating a record of 16 consecutive victories and winning the championship. Yesterday's match against the French Business Association was originally unrelated to the championship, but Donghua should have worked hard to win in order to maintain the undefeated reputation of a perennial winning team. Unexpectedly, against all expectations, the game ended in a 3-3 draw amidst dangerous situations. In the first half, Donghua took a 2-1 lead. The French Business Association has indeed improved, and Donghua's performance has declined compared to before. Since then, it has been unable to obtain a completely new record.

The Enemy's Fierce Momentum Leads to Loss of Territory 187

The French Business Association first had the right to kick off. Donghua intercepted it. Chen Yutian once charged straight along the side, but it was ineffective. The French Business Association immediately began the order to launch a general attack. The army advanced and attacked Donghua fiercely. The situation was extremely dangerous. Although Li Yichen once came out of the encirclement, he failed to score. Wan Xianghua had little opportunity to cooperate with his teammates under the surveillance of the enemy. Lu Zhongen changed positions and served as a midfielder. He touched the ball in his own territory. The French Valley kicked it to the center, and it reached the right wing, French Fafanqie. Coleto hooked back and centered the ball, but it was ruled offside and invalidated. Donghua's danger was evident. It had been half an hour. Feng Yunyou kicked a free kick, and the rebound was obtained by Lungeer, who went straight to Fafanqie. The French shot it into the middle, and Lungeer jumped up and charged, and the ball followed into the goal. Donghua's iron gate was lost.

Improvising and Scoring Two Goals in a Row 188

Donghua repeatedly tried to fight back in this slump, but because of the strong enemy, they had to wait quietly for an opportunity. The Donghua players were all smart and quick-witted and could improvise and adapt. Therefore, in the last fifteen minutes of the first half, they broke the enemy's goal twice in a row, and the first half ended with a 2-1 lead. The teammates advanced, and French midfielder Grenell was monitoring Xiao Wan. Seeing the ball flying, he hurriedly kicked back, inadvertently falling behind his own line, resulting in a corner kick. Xiao Wan sent the ball to the center very accurately. Li Yichen saw that the front of the goal was heavily stacked with soldiers, pushed it back, and Feng Zhongjian rushed up and attacked with a strong kick, making it 1-1 and becoming a tie. In an instant of five minutes, Feng Lianyou shot hard, and the ball rebounded. Cao Qiuting deflected it to the left and reached the teammate, who returned to the right. Yu Tian led it and charged straight, not obliquely, beautifully hitting the enemy's goal. Donghua thus took a 2-1 lead in the first half.

Advantageous Situation Suddenly Becomes a Draw 189

Donghua broke through the difficulties in the first half and gained an advantage. The atmosphere was new. In the first quarter of the second half, they added another goal, taking a 3-1 lead. Chen Jiaqiu and Li Yichen advanced in mutual assistance, passing the midfield. Li sent the ball to the right corner. Cao Qiuting returned it to the center. Feng Yunyou rushed up with a kick, and Chen Yutian flapped his hands and flew straight, breaking through three passes in a row, scoring with one attack, making it 3-1. Everyone thought that victory was guaranteed, but it was not so. Five minutes later, the French Fafanqie repeatedly failed to attack on the right. Once he rushed in, Guan Xun'an lost his mind and fell into the rear due to a rebound. Fafanqie got a good opportunity for a corner kick. Coleto, a famous inter-port player, headed it in, and Zhou Xianyan could not save it. The French were overjoyed and recovered half of the deficit. In the last twenty minutes, Donghua's danger did not disappear. Under severe pressure, they indeed lost territory again and became a 3-3 draw. Fafanqie attacked alone, and Li Ning could not stop him. The French had no obstacles after leaving Li and penetrated into the undefended territory and attacked, resulting in a draw and reducing hope. Donghua repeatedly attacked again, but could not change the result.

French Business Association Improves, Donghua Declines 190

The French Business Association had the upper hand everywhere and had a great chance of winning. The two inside forwards, Coleto and Bochet, were the best, worthy of being inter-port players. It is a pity that Fafanqie is old and missed many opportunities. If the ball on the right corner was accurate, Donghua would have been defeated long ago. Li Yichen was the most diminished for Donghua, the connection between the forwards was greatly reduced, and Lu Jin'en was barely satisfactory. The two fullbacks were to blame. It was already fortunate that Donghua was not defeated. The formations of both sides are as follows:

The Actively Progressing Jiangnan Track and Field Team 195

To Compete Against Other Teams at the End of March

And Will Visit Suzhou, Xiamen, Hangzhou, and Guangzhou

The Shanghai Jiangnan Track and Field Team, having returned from Peiping and Tianjin the year before last, originally intended to compete for glory for Shanghai in the National Games. Unexpectedly, the September 18th Incident suddenly occurred, and the Eastern Provinces fell, leading to the suspension of the National Games. As a result, the team remained silent for a long time. Last year, they once prepared to travel to Sichuan, going upstream along the Yangtze River, to promote sports in the various ports of Central and Western China. However, the Sichuan War broke out, and nothing came of it. Now, the Battle of Rehe is raging, and the government has announced that the National Games will be held on October 10th. Adhering to the purpose of strengthening the body to save the nation, the team, amidst the national grief over the loss of Chengde, convened a general meeting of all members yesterday at the Yuebinlou Restaurant. More than twenty people attended, including Hao Chunde, Fu Jincheng, He Debao, Zeng Rongzhong, Dong Shuzhao, Xia Xianxuan, Wang Jihuai, Gong Wanyu, Cao Yu, Chen Jiayou, Tao Yingjie, Yang Qingxie, Zhang Zaojiu, and Xie Xingdao. The meeting was presided over by Wang Fudan, the team manager. During the meeting, all agreed that to save the nation, one must first strengthen the body. Therefore, it was unanimously decided that all team members should start practicing diligently from today onwards, to be pioneers for the nation. It was also decided to have the first competition against another team (the MacLeans Team) at the end of February. If there is a turning point in the war, the team also plans to travel to Suzhou and Hangzhou during the spring vacation, and to Xiamen, Shantou, Guangzhou, and other ports during the summer vacation, to fulfill its responsibility of promoting track and field sports.

Page 16

Free Talk

Random Notes on Poetry by Wang Dao 200

— Gan

"On Human Rights" begins with a parrot. It is said that in ancient times, there was a parrot that flew far away and happened to pass by its own mountain forest. Seeing a large fire there, it dipped its wings in some water and sprinkled it on the mountain. People said that how could its little bit of water extinguish such a large fire? It said, "I have lived here before, and now I have to do my best." (This comes from "Le Yuan Shu Ying," as quoted in Hu Shi's preface to "A Collection of Essays on Human Rights"). A parrot can put out a fire, and human rights can be used to prettify a reactionary regime. This will not go unrewarded. Dr. Hu went to Changsha to give a lecture once, and General He gave him a travel allowance of five thousand yuan. The price is not small; this is "called" experimentalism.

However, how to put out the fire was not very clear during the "On Human Rights" period (1929-1930). After the retail price of five thousand yuan per time came out, it became different. Recently (February 21st of this year), the North-China Daily News published Dr. Hu's remarks, saying:

Any government should have the right to protect itself and suppress movements that endanger it. Of course, political prisoners, like other criminals, should receive legal protection and a fair trial...

This is much clearer! Isn't this talking about "government power"? Naturally, the doctor's mind is not simple; he would not just say, "One hand holds a sword, and the other holds the classics," like some ideologies. He says that one should also hold the law.

Chinese literati who help despots always have this set of ancestral secrets, talking about the kingly way and benevolent governance. Look how humorous Mencius is; he teaches you to stay far away from the place where pigs are slaughtered, while still maintaining a sense of compassion in your mouth, and also having the name of benevolence and righteousness. Not only does he deceive others, but he also deceives himself; this is truly called keeping the mind with principle and reaping endless benefits.

A poem says:

Cultural bureaucrat with a doctorate, human rights abandoned to speak of sovereignty, the court has always been full of massacres, this principle now relies on experimental transmission. Human rights and the kingly way are both renewed, to thank the emperor's grace, I奏for the sage's understanding, cruel politics may as well invoke laws, killing people like grass goes unheard. The gentleman is well-versed in the books of sages, the gentleman's way is never lonely, Mencius has the same heart throughout the ages, also teaching meat-eaters to stay away from the kitchen. A parrot that speaks is more poisonous than a snake, its tiny efforts are boastful, eager to sell its shame to the powerful, five thousand at a throw is not extravagant.

The Fortune Teller 201

— Tang Gai

There is no dawn, and there is no dusk; the world is always without light for him. He does not know what is the expression of human happiness, nor what is the manifestation of human sorrow; his eyes are always a mass of darkness. Every day, he plays the sanxian, walking out of this alley and into another.

The world will never have compassion for him, and he does not even know that there are two words in this world called compassion. Every day, he hears the sound of pedestrians outside the door, and he takes his sanxian, gropes out the door, and goes to the streets and alleys to struggle for life. When the sound of pedestrians on the street gradually dissipates, he puts away his sanxian, walks out of the streets and alleys, and gropes back into his own doorway.

Every day, he plays the sanxian, walking out of this alley and into another.

The strings of the qin vibrate under his fingers, lightly exhaling sighs. He doesn't know why he has to embark on this vast journey. Whether it is morning or dusk, sunny or snowy, he plays the sanxian and just walks, just walking on this vast journey. He is very tired and wants to end this dark journey early, but the whip of life whips heavily, not allowing him to rest. He can only silently hold the sanxian and move forward.

When will he be able to walk out of this dark journey? Only heaven knows.

Visiting People 202

— Zhu Xiang

In "The Unofficial History of the Bureaucracy," it is said that those who are waiting for assignments to visit their superiors must prepare a sum of money as a "door package," otherwise, they will not even have the hope of meeting. I don't know if this situation still exists in the bureaucracy today, because I have never been an official. Most visitors, if they are thrifty, only need to deposit five li of money at the reception desk, which is the cost of a business card. They only ask for this five li of money, which is of no benefit to the reception desk, just like paper money and tin foil.

The best way to visit is to arrange a time in advance, otherwise, between the time the business card is sent in and the time the host arrives, there will be a period of waiting. Sometimes, even if the time has been arranged in advance, this period of waiting is still inevitable. Therefore, I suggest to visitors that, in addition to a business card, they should not forget to bring a book with them, preferably "Lord Chesterfield's Letters." It is important not to bring a book that the host would not like to see, such as "Essays," if the host is old-fashioned, "The Bible," if the host is modern, "Trotsky's Autobiography," if the host is a "Kuomintang member," or "The Three Principles of the People," if the host is a "nationalist." It would be even better if the host himself is an author... The host has arrived. If he waves his hand and offers you a cigarette, it is best to tell a white lie and say that you don't smoke, even if there is an elegant cigarette case or a "Big Cannon Platform" tobacco jar on the table. Acquaintances will take a cigarette on their own; strangers, if they are foolish, will take out a "British Brand" cigarette from the "Big Cannon Platform" tobacco jar. If the cigarette is handed to you in person, then you must act according to the circumstances. If the host knows that you smoke, you have to smoke it out of courtesy, even if it is a "British Brand." If, fortunately, he doesn't know, you can also tell a white lie and say that you don't... but you can't forget to say "thank you" again.

When visiting, you must bring a watch, but you must never look at it in front of the host. If you sit for too short a time, you are afraid that the host will think it strange; if you sit for too long, a disguised order to leave will make you embarrassed. Ah, the pain of visiting, the problem of staying or leaving!

Serving tea and seeing guests off is an ancient etiquette. In the modern era of new trends, the ancient etiquette has been abolished. How to issue a disguised order to leave depends on the host's intelligence. Not speaking; looking at the watch; discussing the weather; asking the visitor's address; and so on. Rickshaw drivers can come in to collect their wages; as for the doorman, he is an inexhaustible source of ideas in this regard.

Then you come out... hurry up and light a cigarette. When smoking, you can comfort yourself: It's a good thing the host wasn't "not at home."

Accommodation and Food for Students Studying in Paris (Continued) 203

— Fusheng

Food

Small hotels in the Latin Quarter only rent rooms and do not include meals. Students living high up in the heavens must descend to earth several times a day for the sake of their stomachs, even when they are not going to class.

The most popular places for students are the prix fixe restaurants. A very ordinary prix fixe meal usually includes an appetizer (Hors.d.oeuvre), a dish of meat or fish, a dish of vegetables, a dessert or fruit, a small bottle of wine or beer, a napkin, and a few pieces of bread (bread can usually be eaten as much as you want). Although the number of items is fixed, the dishes can be chosen by the customer. For example, for meat, there is beef, pork, lamb, rabbit, etc.; just for beef, there is fried steak, braised beef, etc., you can choose one. Although the cooking of this prix fixe meal is not great, the nutrients are very sufficient, and no matter how big your appetite is, you can always eat your fill. When I first arrived in Paris, such a prix fixe meal could be eaten for a little more than three francs, but now it costs five francs (about one yuan in national currency).

If you are not used to French cuisine, or are tired of being stuffed with steak and potatoes, then there are Chinese restaurants waiting for you everywhere in the 5th arrondissement.

Speaking of Chinese restaurants, this is the only thing Chinese people can be proud of. No matter how rude and disdainful the Japanese are towards the Chinese, they cannot help but drool when they see "Chinese cuisine" and praise it endlessly. In Paris, as in Tokyo, Chinese people are not good at other businesses, but only selling this crystallization of five thousand years of civilization—Chinese cuisine—can they still stand firm.

In a corner of the Latin Quarter, there are now more than ten Chinese restaurants. Most of these restaurants are very profitable. Most of the restaurant owners are Chinese laborers who participated in the war. Cooking was not their profession, but because most Chinese people have a talent for cooking, the Chinese food made by these "amateurs" is actually able to attract many foreign diners in Paris. It goes without saying that Annamese and Japanese students have become regular customers of these Chinese restaurants; French people and people from other countries are also very happy to come and play with Chinese chopsticks. Among them, "Shanghai Lou" in particular attracts the most foreign students because it is located next to the University of Paris.

Eating a meal at these Chinese restaurants, if you order à la carte, a single dish, including rice, will cost around ten francs; although "prix fixe rice" is a bit cheaper, the dishes are unpalatable, and two small dishes are not enough for people with a slightly larger appetite. It is really not as cost-effective as a prix fixe meal in a restaurant opened by French or other foreigners for five or six francs.

Since 1929, due to the rise in gold prices, most Chinese students in Paris have been very poor, and very few can afford to eat in restaurants for every meal. Six or seven out of ten use an alcohol lamp to cook something in their rooms to satisfy their hunger. Especially those who live outside the city, because it is inconvenient to eat (restaurants outside the city are usually more expensive than those inside the city), nine out of ten cook for themselves. A few years ago, when Mr. Sun Fuyuan lived in Rose Village, he often went out with a glass bottle to buy methylated spirits; now, Mr. Hu Yuzhi, the editor of the Oriental Magazine, also lived a self-catering life when he lived in a small hotel in the 5th arrondissement. These are all so-called celebrities in China today. The lives of celebrities in Paris are already like this, and the lives of other non-celebrity students can be imagined. However, there are still one or two exceptions among the celebrities, such as a certain bureaucratized art traitor Liu, who, when in Paris, took his beloved wife and children in and out of restaurants such as "Shanghai Lou" and "Wan Hua Lou" every day. But this is ultimately an exception.

The Black Woman's Prayer for God (19) 204

— By Shaw Bernard, translated by Yi Xian

"Only to hand us over to man-eating slave drivers and people-trampling gentlemen," said the black girl. "Lions and elephants share the land with us. When they eat and trample on our bodies, they let go of our souls. When they are full, they don't want anything else. But nothing will satisfy your greed. You make us work desperately for generations, until each of you has more to eat and use than a hundred of us; but you still force us to work harder and longer, while we get less and less food and clothing. You don't understand what you mean by enough; nor do you understand what we mean by not enough. We don't have money to buy the goods you sell, so you always grumble; your solution is just to give us less money. This must be because you worship false gods. You are heathens, you are barbarians. You don't know how to live, and you don't let others live. When I find God, I will have the spiritual power to destroy you, to teach my people not to destroy themselves."

"Look!" cried the first lady. "She's upsetting these men. I told you! She wants to be distant from the sample. Her."

"That inciting nonsense, they are listening carefully. Look at their eyes. That's a little dangerous. If none of you men move a hand, then I'm going to shoot her."

So the lady panicked and really drew her gun. But before she could get the gun out of its holster, the black girl pounced on her and ended her life with just one blow from her beloved "Knobkerry"; she then ran madly into the forest. So the black men couldn't help but be very happy.

"Thank God, her temper has improved," said the first gentleman. "For a moment, things seemed a little bad."

"Now everything is fine. Duke Tou: Would you be kind enough to examine the little brain of poor Miss Fitz-Jones?"

"The mistake we made," said the naturalist, "was not sending her a little of our food."

The black girl hid for a long time, until she was sure that no one was coming after her. She knew she was facing a case of flogging, and that no defense by a black defendant against a white plaintiff was effective. She didn't guard against mounted police; because mounted police were very rare in that area. She didn't want to just avoid the tour group; because this direction and that direction were the same for her purposes, she turned back and walked the way she had come (because the tour group was walking the way she had originally wanted to go), and by evening she felt that she was back at the well where she had spoken to the sorcerer. There she saw a stall selling many statues made of wood, plaster, and ivory; next to the stall, a large wooden cross lay on the ground, and the sorcerer lay on it with his knees bent and his arms outstretched. The stall keeper was carving his statue on the wood very quickly and skillfully. They were watched by a handsome Arab gentleman wearing a turban, who had a scimitar in his belt and was sitting on the well railing, twirling his beard.

"Why are you doing this, friend?" said the Arab gentleman. "You know this violates the second commandment that God gave to Moses. In theory, I could chop you to death with my scimitar; but I am enduring a lifetime of suffering because a spiritual weakness prevents me from calmly killing any animal, let alone a person. Why are you doing this?"

"What else can I do if I don't want to starve to death?" said the sorcerer. "I am the most abandoned person among people. The only way I can live is to sit here and be a model for this kind artist. I lie on this cross all day, and he gives me six pence every two hours. He sells these ridiculous images of me himself and makes a living from it. People play with me as a 'sinner at death' because they don't pay attention to anything except police news. When he has enough stock of statues, and I have saved up a certain amount of sixpence, I take a day off and go around giving good advice to people and telling them useful truths. If they would only listen to me, they would be as happy and good as possible. But they refuse to believe me unless I perform magic for them. When I perform magic, they only throw me copper coins, or sometimes 'tin openers'. They say I am a strange person, they say there has never been anyone like me in the world; but they continue to be foolish, disgusting, and brutal people. This makes me feel that God has sometimes abandoned me."

Spring and Autumn Annals

Wu Proverbs Rendered in Classical Chinese 205

— Zhanlu

Pure Wu proverbs exist in the mouths of illiterate common people. The higher the intellectual class, the more classical Chinese elements are contained in the Wu proverbs they use.

However, in the mouths of illiterate common people, there are occasionally Wu proverbs that have been rendered in classical Chinese. I will write them down below:

The use of the character "zhi" in Wu proverbs is a sign of classical Chinese rendering. For example, "yi peng zhi huo" (a wisp of fire), "yi qiang zhi ge" (separated by a wall), "yi shi zhi shi" (a matter of a lifetime) in ordinary Wu proverbs are all phrases that illiterate people would say. Other examples include "qi you ci li" (how can this be?), "fu zai hu ci" (not caring about this), "fu cheng qi ju" (not forming a situation), "zheng zhong qi shi" (treating it solemnly)... all of these idioms are spoken by everyone. Upon closer examination, every sentence is a classical Chinese rendering.

In the past, when private schools were popular, the books that children chanted inside were familiar to everyone. Often, people who did not know a single character could recite the readings of children. For this reason, some Wu proverbs were influenced by children's primers. For example, when someone ran away, everyone would say "tao zhi yao yao" (peach tree is young); when something was close to being risky, everyone would say "xian xian ling de" (manifesting virtue); and what about being so happy that it's "bu yi le hu" (isn't it joyful?) Eating until it's "yan zai hu ye" (where is it?). These Wu proverbs can still be heard often today, which shows that the children's readings of the past were deeply imprinted in the minds of the general public. These are Wu proverbs that have been rendered in classical Chinese.

There is a contradictory sentence in Wu proverbs, which is that when someone hears the sound of loud crying, they will also say: "ku de bu yi le hu?" (crying so much, isn't it joyful?) Using the words "cry" and "joy" in the same sentence is simply unbearable to analyze closely.

Pawn Tickets 206

— Shiyanye

Shanghai's Prosperity Is Only Superficial

A pawn ticket is a receipt for pawned clothes. Shanghai is an area known as a place where gold is everywhere, so logically pawn tickets and Shanghai people are not related. However, I see so many shops with the large characters "pawn" or "pledge" hanging in Shanghai, whether in bustling areas or quiet places, which proves that this reasoning is inaccurate. Pawning clothes is, logically, an act of the poor, but the fact is not so. There are plenty of people who wear splendid clothes who also have a pawn ticket or several in their wallets.

I once had this fantasy: If I could obtain absolute authority, leading hundreds of people, to impose an emergency curfew on the bustling Nanjing Road, ordering everyone from the Bund to the racecourse, whether in cars or walking, to stand still and not move, then the many people I led would specifically choose people in suits and leather shoes, fine Chinese clothes, and fashionable women, and search them inside and out, layer by layer, checking the deepest part of their wallets. Then there would definitely be many, many people who did not have a single banknote, not a single yuan coin, and perhaps a small silver yuan or not, but only a few yellow, smelly copper coins. In particular, there would be many pawn tickets, found in the deepest part of the wallets of many people, or perhaps more than half of the people would have this thing on them. In this way, what I said above, that people who wear splendid clothes also have pawn tickets, would be proven. How happy would I be to get this proof? However, what would be the facial expression of those who were found to have pawn tickets in the crowd at that time?

This fantasy of mine is also inspired by my feelings, because many of my friends wear suits and leather shoes and fine Chinese clothes. They seem to be members of the bourgeoisie, or at least not poor people, and they always run to the first class when getting on the tram. In reality, they only have a few coins for the fare in their pockets, and the rest are pawn tickets. The four seasons constantly circulate, and their clothes circulate in and out of Changsheng Library (pawnshop), and a wallet is specially bought to be a vault for pawn tickets. One winter evening, I walked past the door of a pawnshop. Two fair-skinned young women in fur coats walked out of the door. They walked in front of me and didn't notice me behind them. I only heard one of them say: "A good silk scarf is only worth one and a half yuan when pawned. Things are really worthless now!" Such beautiful people still go to Changsheng Library, and what is being pawned is a scarf needed in winter, so it goes without saying that all of her clothes for the three seasons of spring, summer, and autumn are pawned. It seems that there are so many pawn tickets in her pocket that she could hold an exhibition. Pawn tickets are not just the property of the poor. I have found confirmation in my friends and that woman. Friends! Have you also seen this kind of person? Shanghai's prosperity is only superficial. I am increasingly convinced of this by the many people who appear wealthy but carry pawn tickets on their persons.

Saving the Nation with Anti-Aircraft Guns 207

— Hua Ling

| On Saving the Nation Through Aviation |

The cry for "saving the nation through air defense" has been echoing these past few days, as high as the Japanese planes fly. Beneath the Japanese planes, like startled birds, the Chinese people are constantly craning their necks, waiting to see the national heroes who will compete to go beyond the borders to "save the nation through aviation" by bombing the Japanese planes, devastating Ye County, and incinerating Chengdu. "Non-resistance" has become a thing of the past. "Prolonged resistance" is a dead end. "Empty talk of saving the nation is useless." "Armed resistance" requires airplanes. Advocating aviation is indeed a crucial plan for saving the nation. "Having a patriotic heart but lacking the means to save the country," even those compatriots who only love the nation with their mouths dare not fail to be moved to tears at this critical juncture, unprecedented in thousands of years, and dig into their pockets to contribute silver dollars to support the century-long grand plan of "saving the nation through aviation." This brilliant plan of "saving the nation through aviation" can indeed make the enemy shrink three inches. However, within a year or half a year, a large number of aircraft will have been purchased, but it is not an easy or ordinary matter to train a large number of skilled pilots in a short time. By the time everything is ready and they are dispatched to Rehe to recover the lost territory in one fell swoop, while on the one hand "saving the nation through aviation" and on the other hand not abandoning "prolonged resistance" and slowly seeking divine help at the last moment, the Chinese people who are stretching their necks in the cellars under the enemy planes will have long been displayed in piles in the dried fish markets of the Japanese archipelago. In my humble opinion, it is better to "save the nation with anti-aircraft guns" than to "save the nation through aviation," as it is more reliable, convenient, and easy to implement. Once anti-aircraft guns are transported in, they can be used, at least avoiding the trouble of recruiting or training pilots when using the "saving the nation through aviation" method. Equip each army with several anti-aircraft guns. When one enemy plane comes, shoot it down and flip it over. When ten planes come, shoot down ten of them and make them crash to the ground. Collect the hopelessly damaged enemy planes and display them, just like the Japanese transported the plaque of "The First Pass Under Heaven" to Tokyo as a souvenir. Repair the better ones and use them for "saving the nation through aviation." "Saving the nation with anti-aircraft guns" is clearly like Zhuge Liang borrowing arrows, isn't that a better deal?

Heartbreaking and Shocking Tales of Turbulent Currents 208

— Ren

Natural disasters and human calamities have engulfed the entire China in a state of absolute depression. Speaking of natural disasters, floods and droughts have displaced countless poor people and buried countless beloved compatriots. The various tragic scenes are too numerous to describe, truly causing immense sorrow and bringing tears to one's eyes!

However, most wealthy people continue to indulge in pleasure, remaining unmoved. Once they themselves encounter disaster, they have the money to flee elsewhere, as if donating from their pockets to help others is not their responsibility. To sit idly by and watch others perish is, without exaggeration, heartless.

Not only that, but some people even use the name of "disaster relief" to fill their private pockets, disregarding the lives of the people. The malice in their hearts is even greater than that of snakes and scorpions.

Yesterday, I went to watch the preview screening of the Mingxing Film Company's production, "Turbulent Currents." I felt that the aforementioned heartbreaking phenomenon had been fully exposed. The plot describes the disregard for the people's livelihood by a wicked gentry, causing one's hair to stand on end in anger. The realism of the scenery is heartbreaking and shocking, as if one were personally experiencing the situation. All my compatriots should watch it.

Long Novel

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 209

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter One

Being Hospitable and Cordial, Especially Inviting a Poor Woman, Remembering the Entrance with Generosity, Particularly Possessing the Ambition of a Soldier

Jiang said: "We mother and daughter shrink in the house all day long, feeling stifled. When Second Master comes, we can chat." Second Master Gan said: "You'll soon have neighbors moving in here, and it'll be lively in the future." Jiang frowned and said: "Lively in the future? I'm worried about that. They are military officers, and we are just ordinary residents. Living with them, I'm afraid we won't get along." Second Master Gan laughed and said: "Speaking of it that way, you seem to have some proud bones. But speaking of it, I'm also a small official, so you probably don't welcome me either." The old girl stood on the side, just smiling and saying nothing. Jiang quickly interjected and said: "What are you saying? If we can't get along with someone like Second Master, what kind of person can we get along with?" As she spoke, the old girl had already taken the package from Second Master Gan's hand. Without even opening it to look, she put it in a broken box by the head of the kang (heated brick bed). Second Master Gan laughed and said: "Old girl, aren't you going to measure the cloth? If it's not enough, and I want you to make me a piece of clothing, you'll have to pay me for the material." The old girl laughed and said: "Second Master, you're not someone who is unwilling to part with an inch or two of material when making clothes. Even if it's short an inch or two, I'll tell Second Master, and Second Master will believe me and won't say that we kept the material." Hearing people say such intimate words, Second Master Gan couldn't help but laugh from the bottom of his heart. Just because the Yang family was an old-fashioned family, and Jiang was present, he couldn't just say jokes casually just because they were poor. So he was still extremely serious, just smiled slightly, and then walked out to the outer room. When he walked out to the outer room, the old girl also immediately said to her mother: "There are no vegetables for dinner yet, I'm going to go to the street to buy two pieces of tofu to eat." As she spoke, she followed Second Master Gan out behind him. When she reached the gate, she laughed and said: "Second Master, didn't you want to drink millet porridge?" Second Master Gan said: "That's right, how did you know?" The old girl said: "This morning, I saw your servant running back from the street with a big pottery jar. He told me you wanted to drink this. We're cooking congee tonight. I'll have the servant bring a bowl to your house to scoop some, okay?" Second Master Gan laughed and said: "Amitabha! You mother and daughter are so frugal, and I'm going to take food from you." The old girl said: "A liter of millet makes a big pot of porridge. No matter how poor we are, we can always afford to send a pot of millet porridge to someone." Second Master Gan laughed upon hearing this and said: "Then I'll definitely bother you." He laughed and left. Upon hearing this, the old girl didn't buy tofu. Instead, she bought red beans and millet on the street, put them in a large pottery pot, and put them on the fire to cook. Jiang said: "Why are you cooking such a big pot of millet porridge? Are you planning to eat it for three days and three nights?" The old girl didn't say anything, but just pursed her lips and smiled (3).

Cicada Draws Out Lingering Sounds, Passing Through Branches 210

— Written by Cheng Xiaoqing

Women's Paradise

Modern Women's Opinions 211

— Huizhu

Women, who have always been veiled by old etiquette, have always adhered to the "golden man's three silences"! Occasionally, there were many talented women who were "presenting memorials like Ban Zhao" and "composing willow catkin poems like Xie Daoyun," but in the eyes of men, they all seemed to be "inauspicious things"!

It was not until the early Republic era when women's liberation was advocated that people realized that women and men should have equal status and the same freedom of speech. In the third year of the Republic [1914], various publishing houses published many magazines about women. The Zhonghua Book Company published "Zhonghua Women's World," the Commercial Press published "Women's Magazine," and there were other things like "Women's Magazine" and "Women's Times." Ms. Lianshi edited "Chinese New Women's World Magazine" in Japan. For a time, it was also quite a sight to behold. Later, the Kaiming Bookstore published "New Women," and the Liangyou Book Company published "Contemporary Women." Places like Beijing, Tianjin, Hankou, and Hangzhou also published women's daily newspapers, women's weekly newspapers, women's guide newspapers, and women's ten-day publications. It's a pity that most of them were "red beauties with short lives," and none of them managed to achieve permanent existence.

It seems that after the January 28th Incident, even the Commercial Press stopped republishing "Women's Magazine," which is especially heartbreaking!

It seems that in the past, small newspapers and magazines edited by general sons all published photos of prostitutes and actresses, but now they are following the trend of the times and using female students as a facade. It is absolutely impossible to compare the noble personality of female students with that of prostitutes. It seems that we female students should protest, strongly reject, and not allow others to publish them. This cannot be regarded as a way to show off!

Especially in practical matters, many of these newspapers and magazines fundamentally lack women's freedom of speech. Since they are called women's publications, even if not all of them must be written by women, they should discuss issues that are closely related to women and serve as a precursor to improving family and society.

Women should no longer be "human puppets" or "social wooden figures"!

Hair Adornment 212

— Ju Yun

"Going to the beauty salon to wash and perm hair." We often hear sisters say this. It seems that they can't wash or perm their hair well at home. It seems that after being adorned at the beauty salon, they can become as beautiful as celestial beings! There are some small studies among them.

Some people soak their hair in water before applying shampoo. Mild water is also added with some borax. However, borax is suitable for soft and shiny hair, but not suitable for astringent and slender hair.

Washing hair must go through the procedure of applying soap lather twice, and each time must be rinsed clean in water. "Rinsing" is just to wash away all kinds of dust, short hair, dandruff, grease, and the like.

After rinsing twice, you can mix half a lemon juice with one ounce of "Hydrogen Peroxide" and melt it in hot water and use it to pour on the hair. This method is suitable for hair of all colors, and the purpose is to prevent the hair from becoming dull, but it is more suitable for people with black hair to use "Sage Tea And Vinegar".

When perming hair, I think "water perm" is better than alcohol perm and electric perm, which can avoid damaging beautiful hair.

If you want to water perm, you have to use Hair Waving Lotion. If you add a little alkali to the hair waving lotion, the result will definitely be satisfactory.

Buying hair waving lotion on the market is too expensive. Here is a simple homemade method:

Potassium carbonate

Half a teaspoon

Rose Water four ounces

Put potassium carbonate in rose water and shake the bottle to make it completely combined.

There is also a kind of "loose hair comb" for water perms. The Water Waving Comb sold on the market is a British product, but imitation is simple and easy.

The result of the hair being loosened into a wave pattern can be preserved for one or two weeks.
