Economic Special Issue

Issue Twelve Published Every Monday

U.S. Financial Panic 213

— Fengwu

America, known to the world as a "Gold Kingdom," has unfortunately experienced a financial panic in its financial sector, affecting the entire nation. We watch from afar, wondering how, despite its abundant gold reserves, this run on banks could occur. Is gold truly powerless to prevent disasters?

This crisis began at the United Guardian Trust Company in Detroit, Michigan, the world's leading automobile manufacturing center. The company lacked sufficient cash to meet depositor withdrawals and the interest payments on loans from the Reconstruction Finance Corporation (RFC). As rumors spread, people became anxious, and depositors rushed to withdraw their funds. Michigan Governor Comstock, on the night of February 13th, convened an emergency meeting with local banking leaders and, with the approval of the Department of Commerce and the Treasury, declared a statewide financial emergency. He ordered all banks, trust companies, and financial institutions to close for eight days, from the 14th to the 21st. As a result, all 420 state banks, 120 national banks, and the stock exchange in the state were shut down. This was the largest economic crisis since the decline of the American economy and has drawn the attention of the global financial community.

Since the crisis began, banks across the country have been rushing cash by train or plane to provide assistance, totaling between 40 and 50 million dollars. Following the advice of Nash and Chrysler, and General Motors, the Ford Company provided United Guardian Trust Company with $20 million in cash, greatly reducing public panic. Governor Comstock stated that the main cause of the crisis was largely due to the panic among small depositors. He said that the suspension order could be lifted once people were assured that their deposits were safe. On the 17th, the Michigan Senate passed a resolution declaring a state of emergency and authorizing the governor to extend the bank suspension period to regulate withdrawals. The suspension of cash payments was also extended to utility bills such as electricity, gas, and telephone, as well as municipal worker wages, which were paid half in cash and half in checks. When the initial suspension period expired on the 21st, the governor ordered all banks to reopen on the 22nd, but only allowed withdrawals of 5% of deposits. Meanwhile, the Ford family took over the First National Bank and United Guardian Trust Company for reorganization. However, because New York banks refused Ford's assistance, the First National Bank's reorganization plan continued to operate under the existing withdrawal restrictions. The trust company was taken over by the Manufacturers National Bank, organized by Ford, which acquired its assets. It is said that a total of 8.25 million gold dollars was invested.

When the crisis first erupted, the entire United States was shaken. Stock market prices in New York and other major cities plummeted immediately. Trading in U.S. dollars was extremely active on the London market, with a particularly large difference between spot and forward prices, reaching as much as 2.5 cents per pound. As a result, American banks profited by buying three-month forward contracts while simultaneously selling spot contracts. The Senate also questioned the actions of the Reconstruction Finance Corporation (RFC), suspecting that it often loaned large sums to banks that were about to fail, and called for a thorough investigation of the company's operations.

Since the bank run in Michigan began, efforts have been made to maintain stability and gradually quell the crisis. However, the result of restricting withdrawals has made people wary. Soon, the crisis spread to Maryland in the eastern United States. A bank run also occurred there. In just one week, withdrawals in Baltimore alone reached around $13 million. Although this was not significant compared to the state's $500 million in deposits, the withdrawal of $6 million on Friday alone was alarming. By the morning of February 24th, there were signs of even greater runs, and two banks were on the verge of collapse. Governor Ritchie convened an emergency meeting of the state's six largest banks and decided to temporarily close all banks in the state for three days to protect the interests of depositors and banks. A total of 205 banks were closed. According to the governor, the foundations of the state's banks were very solid, and only a few were unable to cope with the sudden bank run.

Baltimore, Maryland, is only 40 miles from Washington, D.C., and the financial sectors of the two cities are closely linked. Upon receiving this news, Washington D.C. was greatly shaken, and it was generally seen as a sign of instability in the entire U.S. banking system. There was criticism that the Reconstruction Finance Corporation (RFC) had the authority to alleviate this situation but failed to do so, allowing the closures to occur. It was asked whether this was because the banks in question failed to provide the corporation with the necessary collateral for loans. The Maryland legislature, which already had a bill restricting the amount of withdrawals that could be made without prior notice, quickly passed it in the hope of implementation. However, the situation had already deteriorated, and it was difficult to salvage. National anxiety could not be dispelled, and an unprecedented financial panic intensified and became unmanageable.

After hearing about the bank runs and closures in Michigan and Maryland, the American people's trust in banks was greatly shaken, and small depositors rushed to withdraw their savings. State legislatures also discussed granting governors the power to declare bank holidays to reduce losses for both sides. On the 26th, the legislatures of 20 states convened to discuss this matter. The governors of Indiana, Arkansas, and Wisconsin signed bills to declare bank holidays if necessary. At the same time, New York, New Jersey, and three other states increased the power of the governor to help banks maintain operations and promote improvements. Banks also took precautionary measures. For example, four banks in Kansas, with deposits of $5 million, merged with the Commerce Trust Company. Due to the unfavorable situation, 18 banks in Ohio, with a total of $81.5 million in deposits, declared a suspension of payments on the 27th. The Dayton City Council convened an emergency meeting and immediately declared a bank holiday. However, the state legislature passed a law allowing banks to restrict withdrawals in emergencies to prevent bank runs, but only with the approval of the State Banking Commission. As a result, banks in Dayton, Akron, Lima, Cleveland, and other cities reopened under withdrawal restrictions. The Pennsylvania legislature also allowed banks to independently determine withdrawal restrictions without the approval of the state.

Despite these measures, public confidence had already been undermined, and the crisis spread further, gradually entering the Midwest and affecting the West. Banks in southern Ohio, Delaware, and Tennessee voluntarily closed for five days on March 1st. California, Louisiana, Oklahoma, Mississippi, and other states successively declared holidays or imposed withdrawal restrictions. By March 2nd, 18 states had declared bank holidays, affecting over 50 million people. More states continued to announce bank holidays and withdrawal restrictions. After the close of business on March 3rd, even New York and Illinois, known as financial centers, could not avoid declaring bank holidays. In the District of Columbia, the U.S. Congress passed a bill on March 3rd granting the President and the Comptroller of the Currency unlimited power to manage deposits and withdrawals in the District of Columbia, in order to preserve the capital's financial hub. The panic spread nationwide. In just the three days, the losses caused by the financial crisis in the United States reached $11.6 million, and the number of banks that declared holidays or imposed withdrawal restrictions reached 3,000. The following is a table summarizing the withdrawal measures implemented by banks in various U.S. states, based on reports from various news agencies. However, due to the brevity and incompleteness of the reports, omissions and errors are inevitable. Your understanding is appreciated. However, all possible effort has been made. (As of the telegraphs on March 4th.)

(Note) According to a Havas News Agency dispatch on the 4th, only four of the 48 states in the United States had not yet declared bank holidays: Montana, Colorado, Dakota (North and South Dakota, one of them has already declared a holiday), and South Carolina. However, Reuters reported that only South Carolina had not. In short, all banks in the United States have fallen into a state of suspension.

The U.S. government's initial response to this crisis was to draft measures to assist in clearing devalued assets when the Michigan run occurred. When Maryland subsequently experienced a run, both houses of Congress passed the Goldsborough Emergency Banking Act, which authorized national banks to assist troubled banks in times of financial emergency. It also granted the Comptroller of the Currency the authority to limit withdrawals of the $17,000,000,000 in deposits held by the more than 6,000 banks across the United States, which was approved by President Hoover and became law. The act granted the Comptroller of the Currency temporary emergency powers for a period of one month, which could be extended with the approval of the President and the Secretary of the Treasury. However, the states already had this power over state-chartered banks. On March 1st, Congress also passed the Frazier-Lemke Farm Bankruptcy Act by a vote of 207 to 26, which was sent to the President for signature. The act allowed debtors to apply to the court for a delay in debt repayment to avoid foreclosure. By this time, the crisis had spread across the country. On the 4th, it was also announced that banks that had already restricted cash withdrawals could receive financial assistance from the Reconstruction Finance Corporation (RFC) if they were in urgent need of funds and had sufficient collateral. (The RFC's requirement that loans must be fully secured has been criticized by some in the financial community, as banks with sufficient collateral would not have difficulty securing loans.) It is hoped that the RFC can be flexible, otherwise many banks will never find an opportunity to borrow from the RFC. President Hoover had planned to convene a special session of the new Congress on March 20th to discuss emergency legislation to address the banking crisis in the United States. The House Banking Committee had prepared to meet and consider legislation. Senators advocated for the establishment of a postal savings system and granting the new President and Comptroller of the Currency the necessary authority to safeguard deposits. The Tennessee Clearing House had developed a method to allow banks to issue their own currency, in denominations ranging from one to twenty dollars, so that depositors could withdraw funds and banks could meet their obligations. There were even reports that Presidents Hoover and Roosevelt had discussed abolishing gold payments or prohibiting cash exports. After Roosevelt took office, he issued a statement to the nation, stating that in order to deal with the ongoing panic, he would ask Congress for full powers, as in wartime, and that he would convene a special session of Congress very soon.

000000000

The impact of this bank run domestically has been that American money, due to depositor panic, and securities have been transferred to Canada. Within the first two days of the month, tens of millions of dollars had moved, causing the Canadian dollar to rise by two cents, and the momentum has not stopped. People with money dare not deposit it in their own country, fearing that it will become dead money. According to the monthly report released by the Federal Reserve Board, the amount of U.S. currency in circulation increased by $134 million in one week, reaching the highest limit. The amount of deposits withdrawn in the past three weeks is unprecedented. Cash reserves have decreased by $116 million this week. Most private individuals are withdrawing deposits, especially in New York, where the total amount of deposits in various banks has decreased from 440 million dollars to 278 million dollars. Recently, all foreign exchange, securities, and cotton markets have also closed, and all industries have come to a standstill. The impact can be described as huge.

Abroad, there was a panic when the Michigan crisis first erupted, but it soon subsided. However, by March 4th, the overseas situation was completely different. The London Bankers' Clearing House Committee decided to suspend all foreign exchange transactions. According to news from major European ports, the number of ports suspending foreign exchange transactions increased. Only the British pound was traded in Dalian, and there was no U.S. dollar market in Paris, and banks did not honor U.S. bank checks. Rome suspended U.S. dollar trading for two hours. The Italian National Bank wired New York banks to convert all deposits into gold accounts, fearing that the United States might ban gold exports and repeat the United Kingdom's abandonment of the gold standard.

000000

The reason for the severity of this financial crisis in the United States is unknown even to American banking experts. Although it started in Detroit, the situation there had calmed down when it broke out in other cities. As the crisis intensified, between February 25th and 28th, it created the current situation of nationwide bank closures. There is no other reason than that the beginning of the crisis was subtle, and when the public heard that the banks experiencing runs were closing, they were afraid of being affected and rushed to withdraw their deposits from the banks to prevent unforeseen circumstances. The more intense the panic among depositors, the greater the risk to the banks, and the banks were unable to cope, leading to closures. Banks closed in one place and depositors became even more panicked. Everyone thinks only of immediate gains and not of the losses after banks collapse. No matter what governments and police warn, they cannot stop depositors from withdrawing money. At this time, the psychology of depositors has become abnormal. They are just afraid of being left behind and not being able to withdraw their deposits. This is not only true for banks. Even companies with solid foundations are sometimes forced into bankruptcy due to the lack of cash flow, as the banks and money shops tighten their grip. Banks accept deposits, but in addition to setting aside a certain amount of cash as reserves, the rest is circulated to industries and businesses. There is no reason to hoard large amounts of cash, so if depositors rush to withdraw money beyond the normal reserve, the banks will naturally be unable to cope and will not be able to immediately recover their loans. If one bank experiences withdrawals, other banks can provide assistance. However, now that most banks in the United States are experiencing withdrawals, the only option is to temporarily close. Rumors spread rapidly. This shows the panic of the people and that disaster often arises from small things.

The underlying cause is still the impact of the global economic recession. Since most countries abandoned the gold standard, the United States has maintained the status quo. As a result, foreign trade is clearly unfavorable. Internally, there is overproduction, falling prices, economic downturn, increased unemployment, and hardship for the people. For example, cotton prices have fallen to one-fourth of what they were three years ago, and wheat and pork prices have fallen to one-third. Farmers, workers, and businesses are all suffering from this serious impact. In order to increase domestic prices and restore export trade, Borah advocated (1) resolving the war debt issue (as long as it is not resolved, U.S. financial resources will be reduced); (2) currency inflation to raise prices; (3) reducing government spending (U.S. government spending has expanded, such that every minute spent requires over $2,300 and that every person works four months a year to support the government); (4) changing the value of currency, establishing a bimetallic standard of gold and silver, raising the price of silver, and reorganizing private debt to eliminate panic. However, this was disliked by Republicans. In his farewell address, President Hoover said that the United States had reached a crossroads in the economy. The first path is for countries to cooperate, remove barriers to world trade, and eliminate obstacles to raising prices. This is the path to immediately relieve agriculture and reduce unemployment worldwide. The second path is for the United States to rely on its vast territory and resources, increase tariffs. The third path is to inflate the currency, abandon the gold standard, and enter a global economic war, but the result will inevitably be mutual destruction. However, since the Democratic Party came to power, the financial industry has experienced an unprecedented panic, and Hoover's words may change.

American banks have been affected by the aforementioned factors, and the goods and assets they hold have depreciated due to economic inadequacy or falling prices. As a result, they have lost the trust of depositors, and the bank run is rooted in this. What the future holds remains to be seen. March 4th, Year 22.

Commentary on National Coinage Design 214

— Pan Shihao

National coinage must possess appropriate design, including its pattern, diameter, weight, fineness, and other virtues. The diameter, weight, and fineness of our national coinage are all clearly stipulated by law. With the exception of the silver coins of the Qing Dynasty, patterns are typically defined by edict. This aspect of design holds considerable value for research, leading to the emergence of a discipline known as "Heraldfytty" [likely a misprint for "Heraldry"]. Through these designs, we can discern various manifestations of a nation's character, encompassing the political systems of the time, changes in religious beliefs, the flourishing or decline of aesthetic values, the waxing and waning of customs, and the rise and fall of cultural artifacts and craftsmanship. Though seemingly a minor detail, it is intrinsically linked to a nation's honor and standing.

The designs of our national coinage, from the dragon of the Qing Dynasty to the Yuan Shikai portrait of the early Republic, the commemorative coins of the founding of the Nationalist government, and the newly announced coinage of the Central Mint, have undergone several changes. Are these new designs progressive, regressive, rational, or irrational? Let us examine them separately.

(1) The Birth and Death of Minting Locations: National coinage, being a form of currency universally used throughout the country, should only bear the name of the nation, without specifying the location of minting. This is a common principle among all countries. During the Qing Dynasty, numerous mints were established, resulting in multiple coinages, with each coin bearing the name of the province in which it was minted. This was a flaw. The Yuan Shikai coinage of the early Republic eliminated this defect, and the new national coinage follows suit. This is a point of progress.

(2) The Birth and Death of Weight and Relative Value: The weight and relative value of national coinage are invariably specified by law in all countries. Mints adhere to these laws during production, and the public relies on them during transactions. Such regulations are considered essential and inviolable. Various Qing Dynasty coinages were deficient in this regard, resulting from lingering irrational customs. Since the establishment of the Republic, there has been considerable effort to eliminate these flaws, freeing up coin design from unnecessary complications. This represents a second point of progress.

(3) The Emergence and Vanishing of Foreign Languages: National coinage differs from trade currency. National coinage represents the nation itself, and as such, should not feature any language other than the national language. Trade currency, on the other hand, is specifically designed to facilitate trade and may include foreign languages. When Zhang Zhidong was initially granted permission to mint silver dollars during the Qing Dynasty, the intention was to counter the influence of Mexican silver dollars, which included both Chinese and foreign languages to facilitate trade with foreign countries. This was essentially a form of trade currency. However, in practice, weighing was still used in both Chinese and foreign transactions. In international trade, silver dollars were simply considered raw silver, and the inclusion of foreign languages had no practical value. Later, various provinces began minting silver dollars, and the national coinage status of silver dollars was formally established by the regulations governing silver coinage. However, the inclusion of foreign languages in the design persisted. The Yuan Shikai coinage alone eliminated this defect, which must be considered a significant improvement. The commemorative coins of the founding of the Nationalist government reverted to the use of foreign languages, purportedly because these coins were different from ordinary coins and were intended to be displayed both domestically and internationally. However, the inclusion of foreign languages on national coinage is somewhat flawed. Recognizing this, the new national coinage completely omits foreign languages, which constitutes a third point of progress.

(4) The Merits and Demerits of the Obverse Pattern: In addition to the aforementioned points regarding the birth and death of design elements, the patterns themselves are also worth discussing. The obverse of the new national coinage features a profile portrait of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, with the dignified inscription "Republic of China, Year Twenty-One" above it, which is perfectly suited to the national identity. Whether judged by national policy, historical context, or the preferences of the national character, this portrait is well-suited to representing the nation. It represents a significant improvement compared to the superstitious dragon of the Qing Dynasty, or the Yuan Shikai portrait which betrayed an imperial autocracy. This is the fourth point of progress.

Historically, the portraits on coinage have generally been idealized, such as the use of the Statue of Liberty in the United States. Alexander the Great initiated the practice of using his own portrait on coinage, setting a precedent for using contemporary figures on coin designs. However, this practice is not ideal. Yuan Shikai, as the head of a republic, embraced the imperial autocracy's concept of "I am the state," attempting to use himself, a single individual, to represent the nation. This was a delusion. Sun Yat-sen, however, was the pioneer of the founding of the nation and the precursor of the Three Principles of the People. Everyone who knows China knows about Dr. Sun, and every Chinese citizen reveres Dr. Sun. The use of his portrait on coinage as the design of national coinage is vastly different in its impact on the national character. The effects on the national character, and the impact on the national psychology, are incommensurable.

(5) The Merits and Demerits of the Reverse Pattern: The reverse of the new national coinage features the rising sun, a sailboat setting forth, and seagulls soaring above the sea, with the characters "One Yuan" inscribed on either side. The design is dynamic and full of vitality, well-suited to promoting the spirit of development and progress. In this time of national crisis, fraught with internal and external threats, such a design is particularly appropriate. The reverse of the commemorative coins of the founding of the nation features stalks of grain, as does the Yuan Shikai coinage. Since our nation is founded on agriculture, and grain represents prosperity, such designs are unobjectionable. However, in terms of dynamism and progress, the new coinage is superior. If the people of the nation can be inspired to become self-reliant and shed the lethargy and stagnation of the past, this national coinage can truly represent the modern national character. This constitutes a fifth point of progress.

In conclusion, the designs of the new national coinage lack superfluous or useless patterns and characters. They are well-suited to representing the national identity and promoting the national character. The characters are limited to the name of the nation, the year, and the denomination. The patterns, in addition to the aforementioned rational points, are free of any disjointed or fragmented elements. The commemorative coins of the founding of the nation can be considered progressive in design, but they feature foreign languages on the reverse and superfluous floral ornaments on either side of the obverse. The new national coinage surpasses them in its improvements. The ingenuity of the designers deserves our gratitude.

While the design of the coinage is important, strict quality control during minting is essential to prevent wear and counterfeiting. Regular and public chemical assays of the weight and fineness are necessary to maintain the credibility of the national coinage. It is hoped that the minting authorities will pay close attention to this.

Securities Market Detached from the Situation Last Week 217

Too Many Shorts Feeling Insecure

Several Issues Unmoved, Large Increases Over Two Days

From February 27th to March 4th of last week, the public bond market of the Chinese Merchant Securities Exchange saw no trading on February 27th due to the settlement of February futures contracts, resulting in only five days of trading. Initial trading was slightly volatile, followed by large increases over two days, ultimately ending in a pullback. Amidst unfavorable news from the Rehe front and increasingly tense rumors in Peiping and Tianjin, the general public expected bond prices to plummet due to the urgency of the external threat. Most focused on shorting, leading to an increasing number of short positions. However, the longs seemed weak, and poised to waver. But after the settlement, there was no selling off. This revealed that capitalists were a backbone. Short sellers covered their positions due to a lack of hope. The increase in the foreign market was detached from the current situation, but this was not by chance. A breakdown of each day’s trend follows.

(Tuesday) The first day after settlement, the market heard the government was appropriating 20% of bond funds for war expenses, retail investors sold short, and big players bought low, making prices weaken slightly, 3 to 5 jiao, contrary to shorts' expectations.

(Wednesday) The rumors of Japanese attacks on Tianjin intensified, and inexperienced investors shorted further. Prices were soft from morning to evening, but supply and demand were balanced, and the market only dropped slightly, 3 or 4 jiao. The salt tax also rose 2 jiao. Short sellers gradually shifted, anticipating a short squeeze, as the attack on Tianjin had not materialized.

(Thursday) Northern investors were the first to see the opportunity and began to cover their positions amidst the tense wartime atmosphere. Prices steadily rose, leaving retail short sellers in a dilemma.

(Friday) Suddenly, news broke that three Chinese representatives in Geneva had resigned. Savvy retail investors took the opportunity to cover their short positions, and prices fell before rebounding. Northern buyers were particularly aggressive, and the market rose another yuan.

(Saturday) Due to high prices, real goods were sold, causing early trading to rise, but the market could not sustain momentum. Some longs took profits, leading to a pullback, falling 7 or 8 jiao.

Overall, longs profited from the week. The main reason for the rising trend was too many retail short sellers, while large long positions remained unchanged. A lack of supplies in the market led to the unusual situation that was opposite of the current crisis. As a result, the bonds continued to rise by several jiao to over one yuan compared to the previous week. The total trading volume was 30,175,000 yuan. Hangzhou Municipal Government Implements

Improvement of Mulberry Planting and Silkworm Rearing in Urban Areas 219

Setting up the Silkworm and Mulberry Improvement Association, to be Established on the 15th of This Month

In light of the deteriorating state of silkworm and mulberry cultivation in the urban areas, the Hangzhou Municipal Government has initiated the organization of a Silkworm and Mulberry Improvement Committee. Representatives appointed by the Municipal Government, as well as district chiefs from various districts, and silk-related organizations, will serve as ex-officio members. In addition, individuals with extensive knowledge and experience in the silkworm, mulberry, and silk industries will be invited to serve as specialized committee members to jointly devise solutions. The committee will have two sections: propaganda and guidance. Five executive committee members will be elected by the members. The official establishment is scheduled for the 15th of this month. It is reported that He Shangping, a technician from the Shanghai Joint Silkworm and Mulberry Improvement Association, and Chu Fucheng, a leader in the silk cocoon industry, have both been invited to serve as specialized committee members. A preparatory committee will first be held in Hangzhou tomorrow (Tuesday) to discuss implementation methods for improving silkworm rearing, mulberry planting, and related matters.

Hardware and Cement Prices Plunge by Fifty Cents 220

Cement Market: Since the establishment of domestic cement companies such as Qixin and Huashang Taishan, shipments have been smooth and sufficient. Foreign brands like Qingzhou Asano Jianglong have been phased out, and merchants can no longer come to Shanghai. In the last 5 or 6 years, the cement market in this city has been controlled by the Chinese. However, in the beginning, the companies competed with each other, and the prices went down. After there was coordination, each company agreed to raise prices (the name is: National Cement Company), so for the past three or four years, the price has not changed. However, the price decreased by 50 cents yesterday, which surprised many people. According to investigations, each company has different opinions, so they are separating in an intangible way. Thus, prices in the coming days are likely to differ. Currently, a horse brand cement bucket is priced at 4 liang and 5 qian (unchanged), while a bag is priced at 3 liang and 4 qian and a half (dropped 50 cents). Elephant brand cement buckets are also priced at 4 liang and 5 qian, while bags are priced at 3 liang and 4 qian (both with an additional factory tax of 6 jiao). It is reported that transactions have recently decreased, presumably because buyers are adopting a wait-and-see approach.

Page 19

Zhang and He Confer on Recovery Plan

Our Troops Outside Gubeikou Have Advanced on Multiple Fronts. Enemy Aircraft Bombing at Xifengkou and Gubeikou. Zhang Xueliang to Depart for the Front to Supervise the War.

(Peiping) Zhang Xueliang and He Yingqin spent a long time last night discussing the recovery plan. In addition to severely punishing those responsible for defending the territory, Zhang has decided to depart for the front line to command and supervise the counterattack, determined to fight the enemy to the end. (6th Special Dispatch)

(Peiping) Our troops outside Gubeikou have built solid trenches. The morning before, our troops advanced on multiple fronts in a counterattack. The left wing reached Qing Shi Lin, and the right wing crossed Anjiang Camp, advancing along the Han'erling Ridge. Commander Sun Zhengfang is commanding at the front line. It is reported this morning that they have already made contact with the enemy. (6th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) On the morning of the 6th, enemy aircraft continued to bomb Gubeikou, Xifengkou, and other locations. Our troops' new defense line along the Great Wall has been established and is ready for a counterattack within days. (5th Special Dispatch)

(Peiping) He Yingqin telegraphed the Central Government yesterday, requesting a clear order to strip Tang of his position and investigate him. Tang plans to flee to Dolon Nor, and it is reported that a unit has been dispatched to intercept him. (6th Special Dispatch)

(Peiping) The Rehe Provincial Government has been changed to the Kawabara Brigade headquarters. Traitor Zhang Hai Peng has arrived in Chengde. The Japanese plan to transform Rehe into the Xing'an Province and appoint Zhang Hai Peng as chairman. (6th Special Dispatch)

(Peiping) The area around Lengkou, Lulong, and Qian'an is heavily guarded. The Japanese have already made preparations at various points along the Great Wall. News reports indicate that an advance unit of Japanese troops has arrived at Lengkou, intending to block the retreat of our troops at the front. (6th Special Dispatch)

(Peiping) Chiang's telegram arrived in Peiping tonight, ordering the Northeast Army to continue resisting. Zhang Zuoxi's troops at Gubeikou, Wan Fulin's troops at Pingquan, and Sun Dianying's troops at Chifeng were concentrated and divided into five routes to counterattack Chengde. Upon receiving Chiang's telegram, Zhang ordered the front-line troops to concentrate at strategic locations for a final stand. Japanese advance teams moved towards the Peiping-Rehe highway. Small numbers of enemy troops have been spotted near Kalatun and have made contact with our troops. Our troops have built solid trenches twenty miles northeast of Gubeikou, using Great Wall bricks and stones. Defensive works have also been built in the Anziling area. (5th Special Dispatch)

(Peiping) A Reuters special correspondent, reporting from Gubeikou, said that yesterday he saw Tang Yulin traveling lightly in a car towards Gubeikou. Yesterday, Japanese planes bombed Gubeikou, but there were no casualties. Temporary field hospitals are visible along the road to Gubeikou, and the staff in each hospital are very busy treating the wounded. The entire city of Gubeikou is crowded with soldiers and civilians. Today, a regiment of reinforcements entered Rehe, establishing a defense line twenty miles inside the border to block the Japanese advance. (6th Reuters Dispatch)

(Peiping) There is still fighting on the Rehe front today. The Chinese troops in Rehe are currently retreating in three directions: one group is retreating west from Chifeng into Dolon Nor in Chahar; one is concentrating at Gubeikou from Chengde; and one is retreating to Xifengkou from Lingyuan. These Chinese troops are constantly threatened by Japanese aircraft during their retreat, so their movement is extremely rapid. At the same time, Japanese aircraft are preventing Chinese troops from advancing towards Chengde because the number of Japanese troops in Chengde is still small. The Japanese troops who entered Chengde yesterday received reinforcements from the Suzuki Brigade in the afternoon. Although Zhang Xueliang's troops have suffered many casualties, they are still willing to fight. They may engage in another fierce battle between Chengde and Gubeikou. The 60,000 Chinese troops currently concentrated at Gubeikou have been ordered to advance twenty miles into Rehe and are building new positions there. Zhang Xueliang's direct troops, numbering 20,000, participated in this battle in Rehe, and the whereabouts of most of them are now unknown. Tang Yulin's troops are currently retreating in a disorderly manner, and many boxes of ammunition have not yet been opened or unloaded, but are being transported back by camel convoys. Zhang Xueliang received a telegram from Chiang Kai-shek ordering him to continue fighting. All the troops in the province have been strictly ordered to fight. Song Ziwen and other government leaders will soon arrive in Peiping to take charge of everything. Tang Yulin's whereabouts are still unclear. Today, Zhang Xueliang's spokesman firmly denied rumors that Chahar had been in contact with the "Manchukuo" about annexation, and said that Chahar is currently making military preparations within its provincial borders and will defend itself by force if Japanese troops invade. (6th Reuters Dispatch)

(Peiping) According to this morning's communique, Wan Fulin has established his headquarters in Kuancheng and has ordered a counterattack on Pingquan. The news of Japanese aircraft bombing Gubeikou and flying to Xifengkou has been confirmed. (6th Reuters Dispatch)

Sun Dianying Determined to Defend the Hunting Grounds to the Death 221

(Nanjing) Sun Dianying telegraphed the Central Government on the evening of the 5th, reporting on the recent combat situation and stating that he would cut off the Japanese advance south in the area around the hunting grounds. He hopes that the Central Government will quickly order the generals at Gubeikou to counterattack Chengde, and his troops will also counterattack Chifeng. If there are no orders from the Central Government, he is determined to defend the hunting grounds to the death. (6th Special Dispatch)

Ding Brigade Battalion Commander Wounded and Arrived in Peiping 222

(Peiping) Jing Youzhang, the battalion commander of the Ding Xichun brigade, was wounded and has arrived in Peiping. According to him, the 8th Brigade was ordered to proceed to Lingnan and set up three lines of defense at Shaomao Mountain, Baishizui, Matihugou, and Benniuyingzi. The Japanese army launched a general offensive on the 22nd, using armored vehicles and small tanks to charge forward, covering the advance of the infantry. The enemy's artillery fire was extremely fierce. Our officers and soldiers fought bravely and resisted until the 26th, when the Japanese Allied Forces' main force from Chaoyang launched a fierce attack on our rear. Our troops retreated and defended the last ground at Mangniuyingzi. They encountered the Japanese army on the way, and the enemy attacked fiercely with artillery and tanks. All three of our regimental commanders were directing the battle on the front line. He himself was shot and wounded. Regimental Commander Chen was still supervising the battle when a tank crashed into and injured him. He was carried from Matihugou to Qinhuangdao and then to Peiping. (5th Special Dispatch)

Situation Before Tang Left Chengde 223

(Peiping) Those who escaped from Chengde say that one night Tang heard that Cui Xingwu had already reached a compromise with the rebel Shao Benliang and was preparing to surrender to the puppet state. Tang immediately asked Cui about this via long-distance telephone. The reply was, "You owe me wages and don't pay them, so there's nothing else to talk about." On the morning of the 2nd, Tang convened a meeting of important officials of the Rehe Provincial Government and representatives of local organizations. Tang expressed his determination to leave Rehe. After the meeting, he received a telegram from Zhang ordering him to hold firm. Tang then ordered Tang Yuming of the 19th Artillery Regiment to lead his troops to hold the Hongshilaling, nine miles from Chengde. After Tang's regiment arrived at that location, they demanded unpaid wages. Tang ordered that each person be given two yuan, but they refused. He then increased the amount to two yuan, but as soon as the money was distributed, a mutiny erupted, and the troops scattered. The rest also deserted. (5th Special Dispatch)

Wan Fulin Telephones Report Arrived at Kuancheng 224

(Peiping) Wan Fulin telephoned Peiping, stating that his troops had been surrounded and fiercely attacked by the enemy on the morning of the 5th. A certain adjutant was killed by a bullet. He himself went to Kuancheng. (6th Special Dispatch)

Cui's and Liu's Troops Unite 225

(Peiping) Cui Xingwu's and Shi Wenhua's two brigades are now united with Liu Guitang's troops guarding Tianshan in Lindong and Linxi. On the 3rd, they engaged in a fierce battle with Motegi's troops of 4,000 to 5,000 men for five hours. The enemy retreated, and our troops are now in pursuit. (6th Special Dispatch)

Fierce Fighting Continues Southwest of Lingyuan 226

(Peiping) Division Commander Miao Zhengliu telegraphed Peiping, stating that his troops and Shen Ke's division are currently engaged in fierce fighting with more than a thousand enemy troops in the area of Lamadong and Shuiquanzi, southwest of Lingyuan. He is determined to defend that position to the death. (6th Special Dispatch)

Tang's Family Has Arrived in Tianjin 227

(Tianjin) Tang Yulin's family arrived in Tianjin from Chengde on the evening of the 5th, bringing with them thirty-eight boxes. (6th Special Dispatch)

(Peiping) Tang Yulin, who retreated to Fengning, later continued north from there, seemingly fleeing towards Dolon Nor in Chahar Province. His troops have already scattered. Furthermore, according to a telegram from Fengning, Tang Yulin, who fled to Fengning, arrived in Fengning County this afternoon. Of the 2,000 soldiers he brought from Chengde, all but 150 deserted along the way. Tang has nothing left, except for his main wife and five concubines. (5th Dispatch)

Guangdong, Guangxi, and Fujian Determined to Send Troops to Support Rehe 228

Cai Tingkai Appointed Commander-in-Chief of the Allied Forces

Bai Chongxi Will Also Travel with Cai

(Xiamen) Confirmed news: Guangdong, Guangxi, and Fujian will each send a division to support Rehe. After the decision was made, Cai issued an order on the 5th for each division to send one regiment. In addition, the two training regiments and the supplementary brigade will each send a regiment, for a total of six regiments. They set out on the 5th to concentrate in Huanggang, travel via the Dongjiang River, and take the Yuehan Railway to join the two divisions from Guangdong and Guangxi. Cai Tingkai has been appointed commander-in-chief of the allied forces and will depart soon to lead the troops. Bai Chongxi will also travel with him. Tan Qixiu, who was originally recuperating, entered Zhangzhou with great effort on the afternoon of the 5th. (5th Special Dispatch)

Japanese Troops Continue to Arrive at Shanhaiguan 229

Rumors of Provocations on the Shi River Front

(Peiping) A train of Japanese troops and a train of armored vehicles arrived at Shanhaiguan and stopped at the Shanhaiguan station. They carried 600 to 700 soldiers who were stationed in the Japanese barracks and in the city. It is widely rumored in Shanhaiguan that because the Japanese have been successful in Rehe, they are planning to provoke incidents on the Shi River front. However, our side is well-prepared. (6th Dispatch)

(Peiping) The Japanese Second Fleet has been ordered to sail to Qinhuangdao, and the Japanese Third Overseas Dispatch Fleet has been ordered to move towards the Yangtze River. The Japanese aircraft carrier that arrived at Qinhuangdao a few days ago is now anchored thirty miles offshore. (5th Special Dispatch)

(Peiping) Public reports state that the situation in Shanhaiguan is very tense, with trains continuing to transport Japanese troops to Shanhaiguan. Japanese aircraft are monitoring the Chinese army's front lines daily. It is said that a large number of troops arrived in Shanhaiguan yesterday. (6th Reuters Dispatch)

Luo Wengan Expresses Determination Not to Be Passive 230

(Nanjing) During the memorial service at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the 6th, Luo Wengan reported that the national crisis is now even more serious, but the more difficult it is, the more we must struggle. Since returning to office last year during the January 28th Incident, he has been committed to the spirit of struggle. Although he is not feeling well, he has never taken a leave of absence. He is deeply saddened by the fall of Chengde, but he is determined not to be passive because of this. The news reports that he is being passive are completely untrue. He also encouraged his staff to strive and work hard. (6th Special Dispatch)

Yan Huiqing Arrives in Moscow 231

TASS Moscow, 5th - Chinese Ambassador to the Soviet Union Yan Huiqing arrived in Moscow today.

Important Statements from Military and Political Circles in This City 232

Our Troops in Northern Rehe, Sun Dianying and Weng Zhaoyuan's Units, Have Fallen into Desperate Straits

With No Supplies, No Communication, and Unable to Retreat into Chahar Province

After the fall of Chengde, our troops in northern Rehe, such as Sun Dianying and Weng Zhaoyuan's units, lost contact and were cut off from supplies, causing national outrage. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency went to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters yesterday morning to visit Commander Dai and inquire about his views on this matter. Commander Dai was out on official business, so the reporter was received by Secretary Xu and met with Staff Officer Cheng of the department. According to his expression, Cheng, who is knowledgeable in military affairs, said that the fall of Chengde and the lack of supplies and communication for our troops in northern Rehe have truly put them in desperate straits. Retreating into Chahar Province is very difficult. As for Weng Zhaoyuan, there has been no telegram from him recently, and his whereabouts are unknown. The reporter then visited Central Committee Member Wu Tiecheng at the Municipal Government. According to him, those responsible for the Rehe army's failure to resist for a long time cannot shirk their responsibility. Minister He Jingzhi telegraphed that he had arrived in Peiping, which means the central government has a great determination on this military campaign, and it would not accept any threat from the Japanese Empire. The public order of Peiping and Tianjin will be in safety.

Germany's Armed Election Completed, Hitler's Party Wins Big 233

Long-Standing Parliamentary Stalemate Broken

Two Social Democrats Killed in Election Violence

Reuters, Berlin, 6th – The National Socialist Party and its allies have achieved a major victory in the election, securing 51% of the vote. Hitler's victory breaks the long-standing parliamentary deadlock. Vote counting concluded before 1:00 AM this morning. The known results are as follows: National Socialist Party 288, Social Democratic Party 120, Communist Party 79, Centre Party 70, German National People's Party 52, Bavarian People's Party 20, German National Party 6. The number of seats for the German People's Party and the Christian Social People's Party are not yet confirmed.

Reuters, Berlin, 6th – The final election results were announced around 2:00 AM this morning as follows: National Socialist Party 288 seats, Social Democratic Party 120 seats, Communist Party 79 seats, Centre Party 71 seats, German National People's Party 52 seats, Bavarian People's Party 20 seats, Christian Social People's Party 6 seats, German National Party 6 seats, German Party 7 seats. The National Socialist Party's seat count in the previous two elections was as follows: 230 seats in July 1932, and 195 seats in November 1932. It has now surged to 288 seats.

Reuters, Berlin, 6th – The German general election concluded yesterday at 6:00 PM, and vote counting began immediately. Voter turnout was approximately 80% of the total electorate. The country was relatively peaceful, with only two reported deaths due to conflicts. In the Breslau area, one National Socialist auxiliary policeman was shot and killed, and several others were injured. Police indicated that the shots were fired from a certain house and subsequently fired machine guns from armored vehicles at the house, eventually dragging out all the occupants. In the Affenbar area, there was one death and one injury. In Weimar, a conflict also occurred between National Socialists and Communists, resulting in one National Socialist being seriously injured and nine Communists being arrested. Berlin was calm. Only 41 people were arrested last night, a significant decrease compared to November of last year. However, many Communists were still arrested in various provinces. 20,000 members of the Stahlhelm League marched in formation yesterday afternoon. Crowds cheered them, and they gathered in front of the former Royal Palace, where their leader addressed them before they dispersed. Yesterday, Berlin saw fewer Republican flags and other similar flags, but more flags of the old German Empire than before.

Reuters, Hamburg, 6th – Upon the order of Interior Minister Frick, the National Socialist Party took over the police administration of the Free City of Hamburg today. National Socialists have now taken over the municipal government. The mayor of Hamburg and the president of the Senate have both resigned. The Hamburg authorities have traditionally been a group opposed to the National Socialist Party; this marks their failure.

US Abolishes Gold Standard 234

State Banks Close, Spreading Nationwide

Cuban Banks Also Take a Three-Day Holiday

Roosevelt Calls Special Session of Congress

Reuters, Washington, 5th – Following an emergency meeting today, the US Cabinet announced the decision to convene a special session of Congress on Thursday. President Roosevelt then stated that he is preparing a temporary procedure to address the financial crisis. It is expected that Congress's first action will be to quickly pass a bill to permit the supervision of the national banking industry and improvement of the system, to restore confidence.

Reuters, New York, 6th – The New York Daily News's Washington dispatch stated that, according to a key Democratic figure in the White House yesterday, the United States will abolish the gold standard tomorrow.

Reuters, New York, 6th – Close aides to President Roosevelt predict that banks will close until March 13th to prevent cash from being hoarded or taken abroad. The claim in the Daily News that the United States will abolish the gold standard tomorrow has not yet been confirmed.

Reuters, New York, 5th – Southern California announced a seven-day bank holiday for all banks in the state today.

Reuters, Havana, 5th – Cuban President Machado has announced a three-day bank holiday for all banks, starting today.

Reuters, Washington, 5th – Many places in the United States are considering issuing clearinghouse certificates and the like to replace cash. New York has already printed clearinghouse certificates, scheduled for issuance on March 7th. Treasury Secretary Woodin conferred with important bankers and merchants in Washington today, but the results of the meeting were not made public. News from here tonight indicates that Cuba and Puerto Rico are both affected by the US banking crisis. The President of Cuba has announced a three-day bank holiday, during which all transactions will be suspended. Puerto Rico will suspend bank payments for three days starting March 6th.

Havas, Washington, 5th – Before convening a meeting with the old Treasury Secretary and the banking community, the new Treasury Secretary Woodin secretly consulted with Meyer, Chairman of the Federal Reserve Board. The new Treasury Secretary kept the matter strictly confidential, even refusing to disclose who participated in the meeting. What was discussed is even more unknown. However, it is generally believed that two issues must have been discussed: (1) the Federal Reserve's plan to issue paper money, and (2) the Clearinghouse's request to issue small bills to replace currency. The ban on exports is limited to the domestic withdrawal of cash. The closure of state banks will be for a very short period. We still remember that during the war, the US government defined "those who trade with the enemy" and prohibited the export of cash. Afterwards, Congress did not repeal it. Therefore, Roosevelt can still re-employ this method. It is said that the new Treasury Secretary intends to meet with Roosevelt. After the new and old Treasury Secretaries met with the banking community, some congressmen believed that Roosevelt's speech yesterday seemed to clearly indicate that cash payments would be prohibited. Now foreign countries will not withdraw cash, even if the United States abandons the gold standard. However, for some time, American commercial groups and people have had a strong trend of transporting cash to foreign countries, especially to Canada, and the US government may inevitably prohibit it.

Havas, Washington, 5th – The new Secretary of the Treasury, Woodin, will convene a meeting tomorrow morning with former Secretary of the Treasury Mills, other Treasury officials, members of the Federal Reserve Board, and fifteen important bankers to discuss the banking situation and its relationship to the gold standard. After the meeting, Woodin and other government officials will meet with the new President Roosevelt at the White House. According to well-informed sources, the United States will take extraordinary measures to save the panic. This evening, Roosevelt will issue a proclamation explaining the matter.

US Financial Crisis Impacts Japan 235

Exchange Transactions Suspended, Gold Export Prohibited, Securities Market Shaken

Dentsu, Tokyo, 6th – The impact of the US financial panic on the Japanese economy is being viewed by the financial community as follows: Major exports to the US, such as raw silk, have been significantly affected. Exchange banks, except for the surplus, mostly transfer overseas funds to London. The impact of the panic should not be very great. If the US prohibits gold exports, it will be a major blow. Exchange rate fluctuations are even more expected. There is widespread talk of the US dollar rising to 25 or 30 US dollars. If the US dollar rises to 25 US dollars at this time, the calculation of exports and imports will change by more than 20%, and the securities market will inevitably experience turmoil and be adversely affected.

Dentsu, Tokyo, 6th – Regarding the panic in all banks, the Director of the Financial Bureau of the Ministry of Finance, Tomita, and others still went to the ministry to work on Sunday, collecting information. As a result of the discussion, their unanimous view is as follows: The United States will surely implement the so-called expansionary policy to a considerable extent, but will probably not stop the gold standard. Indeed, a temporary suspension of convertibility may be implemented as a response, but a ban on gold exports is a last resort and will not be implemented until absolutely necessary.

Dentsu, Tokyo, 6th – Due to the impact of the US financial panic, Japanese exchange banks have decided to suspend exchange transactions today. Bank transactions other than exchange will continue as usual. Also, the Tokyo Stock Exchange opened a joint committee at 7:30 this morning and decided to close the market before and after lunch. The same applies to Osaka and Nagoya. Therefore, except for rice, all futures markets have decided to close simultaneously today.

Japan United, Tokyo, 6th – All overseas markets held emergency meetings yesterday due to the economic panic in the United States. As a result, all exchanges except rice have suspended operations today.

Reuters, Tokyo, 6th – All stock exchanges are closed today. If the situation does not improve, they may not be able to reopen tomorrow. Today, all commodity exchanges except the rice market are closed. There are also no foreign exchange rates quoted.

Japanese Troops Stationed in Tianjin Implement Zonal Alert 236

(Tianjin) – Commander Nakamura of the Japanese troops stationed in Tianjin convened a meeting on the 5th and decided to implement an alert starting on the 5th. The area from the Haiguang Temple Japanese Barracks to the Songshima Street Pingyili Intersection is designated as the first security zone; the area from the Pingyili Intersection via Asahi Street to the southeast corner of the city to the gate is designated as the second security zone; the area from the gate via Yamaguchi Street along the river to Mitsui & Co. is designated as the third security zone; and Akiyama Street, bordering the French Concession, is designated as a security zone. Starting at 8:00 PM every night, pedestrians will be inspected, and if necessary, the area will be converted into a martial law zone. All houses bordering the Chinese area may be freely used by the Japanese military to dig gun emplacements and set up machine guns. (6th Special Dispatch)

National Government's Memorial Week 237

Dai Chuanxian Reports on the Intentions of the Japanese

(Nanjing) – The National Government held a memorial week at 9:00 AM on the 6th. Yu Youren, Dai Chuanxian, Niu Yongjian, Jing Tingyi, Zhou Zhenlin, Zhu Jiahua, Wang Yongbin, Chen Shuren, Liang Hancao, Chen Shaokuan, He Yaozu, Huang Musong, Chen Yi, Lu Chao, Wei Huai, and more than 500 National Government employees attended. Chairman Lin led the ceremony. Dai Chuanxian reported, stating that the recent resolution of the League of Nations has made clear Japan's invasion of us, and the right and wrong has been clarified to the world. However, in the past two weeks, Japan's attacks have become increasingly fierce. From before the September 18th Incident to the present, the Japanese have known that their actions are illegal and violate justice, but they still act recklessly. If judgment based on words and justice could make Japan realize, things would not be as they are today. I remember being ordered to go to Japan in 1927 and staying in Tokyo for more than 60 days, giving more than 80 public lectures. After each lecture, I would debate with the audience, and eventually, most Japanese people deeply understood the principles of our party, which were very proper, and expressed great admiration. As I was about to leave Japan, I heard that the Revolutionary Army had recaptured Nanjing, and at this time, the Japanese military authorities suddenly invited me to a banquet. During the banquet, the host gave a toast, saying that they greatly admired the principles advocated by Mr. and the theories of the Kuomintang. Now, your country's revolutionary regime has been listed on the international stage, but there is still one thing to say, that the prosperity of a country does not depend on talking, but on having the power to do it. Japan's existence today is entirely built by fighting. I respectfully propose a toast and wish you all the best. When he spoke, his expression was extremely fierce and cold. This kind of feeling and impression has never been forgotten. The expression at that time had already foreseen the fact of the invasion of our country today. Now the world is clear about the right and wrong of Japan's invasion of us. To make this judgment effective, only we Chinese people can thoroughly make efforts to reach the goal. Especially in the past two weeks, having personally experienced this kind of violence, there is no way to say it nicely. Therefore, I brought up the image of that small banquet in Japan at that time to talk about, so that you know the intentions of the Japanese and their views on right and wrong, based on their own responsibilities and seeing the future very clearly. I hope all comrades will be vigilant. The ceremony was completed at 10:00 AM. (6th Central News Agency dispatch)

Relief Goods from Qingdao Sent to the Front Lines 254

Local Association Actively Raises Military Funds

Qingdao Correspondence: People from all walks of life in Qingdao, with the purpose of uniting to resist foreign aggression, established a local association on the 2nd, electing the chairman of the Qingdao Chamber of Commerce, Song Yuting, and 33 others as members of the committee, and electing Guo Jinnan and 8 others from the committee as standing committee members, responsible for handling all the affairs of the association. On the 3rd, a full committee meeting was held to discuss methods of donating military funds to support the troops. On the spot, donations of 400,000 yuan were pledged, and fundraising is still ongoing. Also, goods for comforting the soldiers at the front lines have been enthusiastically donated by students from various schools and diligently collected by the Goods Relief Association, and have been fully prepared. Yesterday, three railway cars were allocated by the Jiaoji Railway to transport them westward. National Army Destroys Communist Bandits in Eastern Jiangxi 255

Zhu and Mao Flee to Dongshao and Are Intercepted

Hunan Army Recovers Ninggang

Chiang Reissues Bounty Order for Bandit Chiefs

Nanchang Correspondence: The communist bandits of the pseudo 135th Army Corps, pseudo 22nd Army of Zhu and Mao, and the pseudo 10th Army of Fang Shao, and the pseudo Soviet independent divisions stationed in various places in southeastern Jiangxi and northwestern Fujian, concentrated their forces to invade Lichuan last month. After failing, they turned to Nancheng. At that time, the Mao and Li divisions stationed in Liangnan defended the city and fought fiercely with the bandits for more than ten days, finally repelling the bandits. The bandits, unable to succeed, crossed the southern part of Yihuang from the Xiong Village Dangkou and the Ganzhu Kuzhu areas south of Guangchang, and fled southwest into the Dongshao, Luokou, Wangpi, Xiaopu area of the communist nest in Ningdu. After Chiang received the report, he ordered Luo Zhuoying's troops to leave Yihuang Le'an and cut off their route to Ningdu. Recently, the Provincial Government received a winter telegram from the Communist District Party Affairs Office, stating that our army fought the main force of the bandits for three days in Huangpi, south of Yihuang, near Ningdu Guangchang, killing thousands of bandits, seizing more than 2,000 guns, and capturing countless prisoners. Based on this, the bandits' plan to flee to Ningdu failed again.

Ninggang Yongxin in western Jiangxi, bordering Ling County in Hunan, is the birthplace of Zhu, Mao, and Peng. Currently, there is still a unit of the pseudo Third Army, a unit of the pseudo Eighth Army, and the pseudo Independent 12th Division and Guard Division entrenched in the area, led by Li Tianzhu, the communist bandit leader of western Jiangxi and eastern Hunan. They have also recruited scattered bandits from western Jiangxi and eastern Hunan into pseudo independent regiments and guerrilla teams, etc., and often harass the counties of Chongyi, Shangyou, Suichuan, Wan'an, Taihe, Anfu, and Lianhua. It is heard that Chairman Chiang is also planning to advance and suppress the bandits in this area, so he has ordered the Guangdong Army's Li Zhenqiu Division to advance from Shangyou Chongyi towards Suichuan, the Hunan Army's Tao Guang Division to advance from Pingxiang towards Lianhua, and the Jiangxi Army's Wang Maode to advance from the west bank of the Gan River towards the Hunan border, while the eastern Hunan's Wang Dongyuan is also out of the Jiangxi border to intercept. This plan was implemented last month, and all armies have made progress, and the bandit nests of Qixiaqi, Wudoujiang, and Huang'ao have been successively recovered. After the royal army recovered Yamenqian in southwestern Suichuan, the pseudo 22nd, 23rd, and 24th divisions of the pseudo Eighth Army, with about 3,000 guns, counterattacked more than ten times from Xinjiangou, but were all repelled by the royal army, killing more than 300 bandits. The Zhang Brigade of the division captured Cigamping on the border of Ninggang on the 20th of last month, and taking advantage of the victory, advanced and recovered the city of Ninggang, which had been captured by the bandits for six years, on the 21st. The remaining bandits retreated into Yongxin, and Tao's division has already advanced from Pingxiang towards Yongxin to attack them.

Chairman Chiang believes that the bandit chiefs Zhu and Mao willingly fawn on foreigners, so he has reiterated the bounty order, and his order is as follows: [After investigating, bandit chiefs Zhu De and others willingly fawn on foreigners, act as accomplices to evil, harm the country and the people, and have long been wanted. This chairman has been ordered to supervise the suppression and has the determination to eliminate the red bandits and bears the important responsibility of internal pacification and foreign resistance. It is urgent to reissue a circular order, offering rewards for their arrest and clarifying the punishment. For this purpose, it is ordered that the subordinates be instructed to earnestly and strictly arrest them. This order, (1) those who capture the pseudo First Front Army Commander Zhu De and the General Political Commissar Zhou Lai will be given a reward of 200,000 yuan. Those who cut off their heads and offer them will be rewarded with the same amount after being proven to be correct. (1) Those who capture the pseudo First Army Corps Commander Peng Dehuai, General Political Commissar Nie Rongzhen, pseudo Third Army Corps Commander Lin Biao, General Political Commissar Teng Daiyuan, pseudo Fifth Army Corps Commander Dong Zhentang, General Political Commissar Xiao Dongguang will each be given a reward of 100,000 yuan. Those who cut off their heads and offer them will be rewarded with the same amount after being proven to be correct (1) Those who capture the pseudo First Army Corps Political Department Director Luo Ronghuan, Deputy Director Li Zhuoran, pseudo Third Army Corps Political Department Director Zeng Risan, pseudo Fifth Army Corps Political Department Director Xiao Bojian will each be given a reward of 50,000 yuan. Those who cut off their heads and offer them will be rewarded with the same amount after being proven to be correct. (March 3rd)

Measures by Hunan Provincial Government to Prohibit the Issuance of Paper Money 256

Those Already Issued Must Be Recalled Within Six Months

Changsha Correspondence: It is a common practice in various counties and cities in Hunan Province that any company, store, vendor, or household with a little credit can print city tickets and issue them indiscriminately without any restrictions. Once business declines and there are losses, they go bankrupt, harming society, disrupting finance, and having a great impact. The provincial government has repeatedly ordered strict prohibition and circulated orders to all printing offices not to accept printing orders. However, the stores, due to their own interests, do not hesitate to disrupt finance and disregard the law, and continue to issue tickets, resulting in an increase in paper money and a shortage of cash. Therefore, with the recent establishment of the Hunan Branch of the Coin Revolution Association, people suspected that the association was issuing paper money and rushed to transfer cash out of the area, causing panic in the society, a sharp increase in interest rates, and a tight financial situation. After the provincial government repeatedly explained that the association was a private organization engaged in academic research and not an agency issuing paper money, people's hearts finally stabilized. From this, it can be seen that the public's faith in paper money has been lost. Therefore, the provincial government has specially stipulated twelve measures, that all paper money that has been issued and not approved by the Ministry of Finance and the provincial government must be recalled within six months from March 1st. If it is reissued, the circumstances will be considered and confiscated and punished. The order has been circulated to all counties for implementation. The measures are as follows:

Article 1: These measures are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 2 and Article 6 of the Regulations on Suppressing Paper Money, which have been approved for reference by the National Government. Article 2: All printed or handwritten paper money that does not contain the name of the payee and the payment period and is redeemable for taels of silver, silver dollars, silver coins, or copper coins, regardless of the name used (such as wage coupons, circulation coupons, loan coupons, etc.), are recognized as paper money. Article 3: After the promulgation of these measures, all government agencies, silver shops, companies, stores, and households in this province must not issue paper money without the approval of the Ministry of Finance or this provincial government. Article 4: All paper money issued by government agencies, silver shops, companies, stores, and households in this province before the promulgation of these measures, except those that have been submitted to the Ministry of Finance or this provincial government for approval, must be recalled in stages within six months. Article 5: After the promulgation of these measures, no public or private printing office within this province shall accept orders for printing any kind of paper money without submitting it to this provincial government for approval. Article 6: After the promulgation of these measures, in addition to the capital city being investigated and prohibited jointly by the Finance and Construction Departments, each county shall be responsible for temporarily working with the chambers of commerce or township public service agencies in its jurisdiction to ascertain the types and amounts of paper money issued by the public and private sectors, and order them to be recalled separately within the period stipulated in Article 4 of these measures. Article 7: Those who violate the provisions of Article 3 and Article 5 of these measures and exceed the period stipulated in Article 4 shall be fined from 50 yuan to 3,000 yuan. Article 8: Those who commit the offense again after being punished under the preceding article may have their business suspended. The printing office may have its printing equipment detained or confiscated. Article 9: After the promulgation of these measures, the county magistrates of each county have the responsibility to implement

Ma Zhanshan to Return Home, Arriving in Shanghai 257

Deputy Commander Xu Jingde Already Arrived to Meet Him

Xu Talks About the Arduous Anti-Japanese Battles in Heilongjiang Province

According to the Central News Agency, after General Ma Zhanshan left Heilongjiang for Russia, all of General Ma's troops were handed over to Xu Jingde, the acting Deputy Commander of Heilongjiang Province. Mr. Xu recently heard that General Ma was about to return to China. Therefore, he made a detour from Heilongjiang to Shanghai to meet with General Ma before returning to his defense area to plan the recovery of lost territory. Yesterday, a reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mr. Xu at his residence and inquired about the recent situation in Heilongjiang Province. Mr. Xu graciously received the reporter and gave a detailed reply as follows:

Account of Arduous Battles 258

According to Mr. Xu, he is a native of Northeast China and belongs to the military. Since the September 18th Incident, Chairman Ma Zhanshan took charge of the Jiang administration and engaged in anti-Japanese work. Mr. Xu was personally involved in the Jiangqiao and Daxing battles. On the 4th of last month, Chairman Ma went to Heihe to re-establish the provincial government. Soon after, he led the troops to set off. At that time, he appointed Mr. Xu as the Heihe Garrison Commander and Acting Deputy Commander, staying behind to coordinate various routes. For several months, over thousands of miles up and down the Heihe River, Mr. Xu had been trying to advance while defending. The southern route advanced into Nenjiang to spy on Nehe, and the eastern route advanced into Luobei to plan for Suibin. The two routes in the middle were repeatedly attacked by the enemy, but they were repelled. Suibin, a fundamental place, was once recovered, and the defense was consolidated. However, Heihe has always been known as a barren border area, with severe shortages of food and various materials. In particular, the only necessary military supplies, bullets, were not available. Troops and volunteer armies along all routes requested supplies and ammunition one after another, causing a great sense of exhaustion. It took a lot of effort to cope with it for several months, and Heihe became increasingly empty. At that time, Chairman Ma was stationed in Nehe, planning to attack the Harbin station. On one hand, he telegraphed Hailar, Zhalantun, and the Su and Zhang armies to mobilize, and he personally went to discuss strategies, hoping to advance together and recover the provincial capital. However, as soon as Chairman Ma arrived in Zhalantun, the situation changed. Chairman Ma was isolated and unable to return, so he retreated into Russian territory via Manzhouli, hoping to return to China and plan a major offensive.

Waiting for the Opportunity to Act 259

However, after the enemy resolved the situation in Haiman, they concentrated their forces to attack Heihe. Mr. Xu originally planned to concentrate his troops to defend the Xing'an Mountains and fight the Japanese invaders to the death. However, the supplies and ammunition were severely lacking. Although he had the determination to die, he lacked the means to fight the enemy. As a last resort, he handed over the various troops under his command to Chief of Staff Wang and various brigade commanders to be responsible for maintaining order, and secretly instructed them to lie dormant in various counties for the time being, totaling more than 16,000 people, instructing them to wait for the opportunity to act. As for other units, there were still Commander Pu Bingshan, Army of Cai Hongyou, Army of Nan Tingfang, troops of Zhang Xishi, and troops of Xu Haiting, totaling 50,000 to 60,000 people. They were also out of ammunition and food, and their clothing was thin, making it impossible to fight. They were lying dormant in various counties. Xu Haiting, who was not performing well, should be brought to a meeting for disciplinary action. Article 10: 50% of the fines imposed by county governments according to Article 7 of these measures may be used to fund the suppression of paper money, and the remaining 50% should be submitted to the case and taken as a record. Article 11: Matters not covered by these measures may be modified by the Provincial Government Committee. Article 12: These measures shall be implemented after being promulgated by the Provincial Government Committee.

Army Commander Zhang Xishi, due to his advanced age, fought hard in the Laha station and Nehe area for several days. He suffered rheumatism in his arm and has already come to Shanghai for medical treatment. Army Commander Zhang Xishi is also said to have arrived in Peiping, requesting relief.

General Ma to Arrive in Shanghai 260

Mr. Xu heard that Chairman Ma was about to arrive in Shanghai to discuss with the central government and the military authorities in North China a complete plan to recover the lost territories. Mr. Xu disguised himself, changed his name, and made a detour to Shanghai via Vladivostok. He is now suffering from heart disease due to excessive stimulation and plans to recuperate in Shanghai for a while. After Chairman Ma returns to China, he will follow him again to discuss ways to save the situation. However, he regretted that he was a soldier and was responsible for important military affairs, but failed to defend a corner of the border, causing the Heilongjiang provincial government to retreat. He was extremely ashamed. This time, he left in tears, feeling very sad and indignant, so he did not want to express much to the press. He was compelled to give an account of the experience due to inquiries. Chairman Ma has now left Vornosk and should be able to arrive in Shanghai in the shortest possible time.

Shanghai Post Office Stops Sending Parcels to Jehol 261

General Post Office Has Not Received Report from Tianjin Post Office

Suspension is of a Temporary Nature

After the news of the fall of Chengde reached Shanghai, the parcel section of the Shanghai Postal Administration stopped accepting parcels to Jehol today morning, while letters are still accepted, but only a very small number. As of yesterday afternoon, the General Post Office had not received a report from the Tianjin Post Office regarding postal services in Jehol, so the General Post Office had not issued an order to stop sending mail to Jehol. The suspension of these parcels is only a temporary measure. In the future, the items that should be suspended and accepted regarding mail in Jehol will be determined after the Tianjin Post Office reports to Shanghai and formulates methods. According to Kang Yong, a standing committee member of the Postal Workers' Union, the union has telegraphed the Peiping Workers' Union to find a way to evacuate the postal workers in Jehol in batches to ensure their safety, and there should be no danger.

Lang Guanpu Arrives in Beijing This Morning 262

Mr. Lang Guanpu, Acting Chairman of the Heilongjiang Provincial Government and Director of Finance, arrived in Shanghai on the Soviet Russian Tongli cargo ship on the 27th of last month. It is now known that Mr. Lang took a special express train to Beijing at 9:25 this morning to report on the recent situation in the Northeast to the central government.

Mr. Zheng will also report to the National Government and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the situation of the League of Nations and the international situation in Europe and the United States.

A resolution was immediately made to raise funds from members, totaling about 200 pounds in English currency. According to the report, the ship, the Stanleyville, was recently sold to Japan by Belgium and is currently berthed in Wales. Its crew telegraphed: [If the crew is given financial assistance by the Anti-War Association, they are prepared to leave the ship, otherwise they will have no place to live. The crew are all people of color. It is scheduled to leave for Japan at 5 PM tonight. The ship carries a white pilot who intends to join the Japanese Air Force. Reply immediately.] The association, in view of the urgency of the situation, advocated immediate fundraising. As a result, silver dollars and copper coins rained down, and they were carried in trade union flags and men's and women's hats. Representatives were then dispatched to meet with the sailors in Wales with the funds. They will return here tomorrow to report on the negotiations. (April 4, North China Daily News telegram)
