Guo Chengen Talks About the Situation After the Opening of the Mint 268

Five days have passed since the Central Mint opened on March 1. In order to understand the situation since the opening, the reporter visited Director Guo Chengen of the factory this morning to inquire about the factory's output and work situation. The conversation is recorded below:

Trial Period According to Mr. Guo, although the factory has already opened, it is still in the trial period, so the number of coins that can be produced each day has not yet been determined. There are two reasons for this: (1) Most of the required equipment, such as models, etc., are purchased from abroad. The factory now plans to research and manufacture them itself. (2) Most of the workers are newly recruited and are not familiar with coin-making work. Without a certain period of practical training, it is difficult to become proficient. Therefore, although the factory has already opened, it cannot be considered formal due to the above two reasons. Even when President Song came to the factory to inspect the day before yesterday, he believed that it would not be possible without a six-month trial.

Insufficient Expenses The raw silver for making coins is completely delivered by the Central Bank, and the silver coins minted are all made for the central government. The factory only earns a handling fee. Therefore, it will not be profitable unless it produces 300,000 yuan per day. According to my hope, we can gradually transform and increase the minting of silver coins to replace copper coins and manufacture various badges in the future to support the factory's expenses and prevent losses. But things are not easy and cannot be done in a short time.

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Writes to the American Chamber of Commerce Requesting that the US Tobacco Industry Monopoly Be Stopped 269

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce wrote to the American Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai yesterday, stating that on March 3, the Chinese Cigarette Factory Association sent a letter stating that the members of the association's cigarette factories purchased tobacco leaves from American tobacco companies, and the pricing, payment period, and gold and ocean settlement of tobacco leaves were based on the agreements reached with the brokers. Now, the tobacco companies have organized the American Tobacco Association, which uses high-pressure tactics to force the cigarette factories to directly sign trade contracts with the association. If they do not comply, the tobacco companies will stop supplying tobacco leaves. This is close to a monopoly and makes the cigarette factories subject to restrictions at every turn. In order to maintain the factory's operations and the livelihood of the workers, the cigarette factories have to temporarily endure the pain and accept it in order to maintain the status quo, and then seek a proper solution through proper procedures. It is found that the tobacco companies sell goods to the cigarette factories, and even if there are contracts, they are handled directly by the companies and factories, and there is no contract signed with the factories in the name of the association. Even more worrying is that if any cigarette factory does not comply with the association's methods, the association will notify the companies to stop supplying tobacco leaves to the factory. Sales and purchases are originally free, so how can a third party interfere? If the companies change their articles of association or the association has business rules, the association should notify its members to negotiate with the cigarette factories, and both parties should have absolute freedom to trade or not, which has nothing to do with third parties. Now, the association is overstepping its authority and using high-pressure tactics to intimidate with blockades, which is not the way of trade. If this is taken as a precedent, then if there is any dispute between the factory and the company in the future, there will be no way to remedy it by resorting to law. The association, at the request of its members, has already written to the association for an explanation, but has not received a reply. Therefore, we are writing to your association again, asking you to forward it to the American Chamber of Commerce and quickly find a way to correct it together. The practice of the tobacco companies concluding contracts through the American Tobacco Association makes it impossible for the Chinese cigarette factories to compare and choose. The method is unfair. Your association should know that there is no such method in Chinese foreign trade and trade between various countries and China. Your country's tobacco industry is the only one that advocates this monopoly policy, which is enough to cause repercussions in the Sino-US commercial undertaking that has great hope in the future. At present, there are many countries that are dumping at low prices in trade with China. This monopoly policy may maintain its superior position in the tobacco industry because there is still little competition. However, if it loses the sympathy of the Chinese merchants as a result, it is difficult to guarantee that other commodities will not be controlled by this policy. Therefore, the tobacco companies only consider their tobacco business, and your association should consider the overall trade with China. We hope that you will be able to mediate in a righteous manner so that this monopoly policy can be eliminated, which is a blessing for the future of commerce between the two countries. To the American Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai.

Two pistols and 17 bullets were seized. Deng and Chen were shot and seriously injured. At that time, a stray bullet injured a pedestrian, Liu Guoxun. They were sent to the hospital for treatment, as detailed in this newspaper. This morning, the police station sent Wang San and the other four people to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. According to the report of the Chinese and Western detectives, Wang San confessed that he was invited by the injured Chen Zikui to rob the property of a certain family near the Yangshupu Water Plant. At that time, he met Chen on Yangzhou Road, together with the defendants Sun, Yang, and Shi, for a total of six people. Sun Dabao and Yang Dabao confessed that Deng Sanzi instructed them to go to a certain place, so they went together. Shi Youcai confessed that he happened to be going to a friend nearby to ask for money when he suddenly heard gunfire, so he fled and was mistakenly arrested. He did not know the other defendants and did not know anything about the robbery. Judge Wu Zehan ordered that they be remanded in custody and rescheduled to wait for Deng and Chen to recover from their injuries and be interrogated together.

He led detectives Wu Changkai and Chen Hongbin to wait at the bridge on time. A bandit, Zong Huaijiang, was arrested and confessed that his accomplices were hiding at No. 127 Haichang Road. Four people, Li Jinxiu, Li Xiaozhang, Shen A'er, and Wang Changtai, were arrested at that address. Then, together with detectives from the Public Security Bureau, they went to No. 54 Hujiang Road, Zhabei, and arrested two more accomplices, Xia Qirui and Li Wencai. They also went to Yuanyuan Hotel on Fuzhou Road and No. 2 Taopeng Road and arrested Guo Zhengyuan and Shi Jiesan. In total, nine bandits were arrested one after another and taken to the police station for detention. This morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police station lawyer Wang Yaotang stated the above situation, saying that the defendant Shi Jiesan had been punished by the French Concession for illegally trafficking in military supplies in 1928. The police station had not yet investigated the crimes committed by the defendants, so he requested permission to detain them and reschedule the interrogation. Judge Qian Wenqi questioned the defendants briefly and ordered that they be temporarily detained pending further investigation and interrogation.

Talk

Thoughts on the Great Earthquake in Japan 275

— Wu

What a peculiar message! The Kanto region of Japan has had another major earthquake. I guess right! There must be many believing disciples of Guanyin Bodhisattva, so they put their hands together and say, "The net of heaven is vast, and it is not leaky. This is the consequence of murder and robbery!" Others are overjoyed, for the reason that Japan can be greatly injured as a result, and from now on, it may not be able to act recklessly and immediately hit Pingjin! Perhaps the military operation to attack Jehol will stop immediately. As for the gentlemen who are deeply aware of righteousness and work for the country and the people, we cannot accurately guess what they think, because "to measure the virtue of a gentleman with the heart of a villain" is very easy to "lose by a millimeter and deviate by a thousand miles," so it is best not to say it. But for the sake of "neighborly relations between Guo and Mu," perhaps the people of the whole country will be mobilized to save money and food to provide relief. Moreover, when our country had floods a few years ago, the Japanese Emperor "donated" tens of thousands of national funds. Therefore, based on the principle of "reciprocity," it is very dignified for us to reciprocate. Moreover, in the previous Kanto earthquake a few years ago, China also provided a lot of relief. This time, of course, there is no exception. Moreover, the current Sino-Japanese relations have indeed reached a point where it seems that they are about to break down. If we can move people with affection through this, although it may not immediately realize the Sino-Japanese alliance, at least we can avoid using troops, because Japanese imperialism may not have completely lost its conscience, and still will not stop military action.

Everyone has their own saying, everyone has their own reason, everything is logical, so the things in the world cannot be discussed in the usual way.

But in terms of the current form, the situation is indeed tense. Although the newspapers always use large headlines to prominently publish "Shorten the front line due to strategic relations" or "Deploy a new team line." The most clever title is "Entice the enemy to go deep," the name is very pleasant and very hopeful, so that everyone understands each other tacitly, in order to encourage the morale of the people, but to what extent has this morale been actually encouraged? The most obvious thing is that most of the glass windows of the shops are affixed with the four characters "Aviation to Save the Country," so those who really do not have spare money to donate to airplanes cannot avoid being filled with grief and indignation, because what they can take out is only hot blood and heads, but popular armament is actually difficult to do, so in addition to crying out to the heavens, all they can do is to ask the old man to bless them. Now the heavens are "responsive to requests," and Japan has had another earthquake. As for those who hope that Japan will stop its aggression because of the earthquake, so that they can have a rest and wait until "ten years of gathering strength, ten years of training" before comparing their strengths again, we can very well slap them on the buttocks!

However, to put it seriously, Japan's earthquake has nothing to do with us. The continuation of Japanese imperialism's aggression is the continuation of our anti-imperialist war. The broad masses of the people unite and fight to the end with the robbers on the anti-imperialist standpoint.

Correction In the previous article "Why Didn't Matsuoka Commit Suicide," the phrase "only self-help" at the end was mistakenly written as "only suicide." We hereby correct it.

Art and Literature

Mr. Chen Kuilong's Recent Works 276

— Sun Choucheng

Mr. Chen Xiaoshi has been living in seclusion since the Revolution of 1911, residing in Shanghai, entertaining himself with poetry and wine. Although he is seventy-seven years old, he is still full of energy. Yesterday, I saw his recent inscription on Zhang Dingcheng's old friend's three seven-character quatrains on receiving an award in Nepal, which described events of fifty years ago. I could not help but feel the vicissitudes of life, so I especially transcribed them as follows:

The stargate ship returns from ten thousand miles, I sang the sword ring in the sky, I worship the royal envoy again, I personally visit the Himalayas in the remote area.

Famous kings disarm and stop the western expedition, one sentence links the three sides to the heavy and light, the most enviable is the brocade car that follows the crimson festival, and a new alliance is made outside the city of the lady.

Fifty years ago, Ji Zhuangyou, I went to the Zanhuang Building to plan the border, (Guangxu Jiashen followed the Sichuan Governor Ding Wencheng to review the martial arts in western Sichuan, and met the Bianlou), Weizhou wind and rain, Songzhou moon, transport your palm to open up a distant strategy, (Ding Wei supervised Sichuan and managed Tibetan guards, and then moved to Hubei without going to Sichuan)

Mr. Wang's Home 277

— Fang Xin

(1) Fourteen Children

Mr. Wang's home is in a dirty alley. The house is a two-story Chinese style building. In that house, besides Mr. Wang's family, there's also the Zhang family upstairs in the living room, the Huang family in the garret, and the Xue family in the side room. A total of four families live in that small two-story house, and each family has two or three, or three or four children. So, when you go to Mr. Wang's home, the first thing you see is a lot of children. Sometimes they cry, sometimes they fight, making that small living room smoky and chaotic. There are fourteen of them in total, seven boys and seven girls. Strangely, the numbers of boys and girls are exactly half each. The origin of the fourteen children is as follows: the Zhang family upstairs in the living room has one boy and two girls; the Huang family in the garret has two boys and two girls; the Xue family in the side room has two boys and one girl; and Mr. Wang's family has two boys and two girls.

(2) A Half Stool

Mr. Wang occupies a side room upstairs in the house, about two zhang long and seven or eight chi wide. It's not big, but it's not small. Mr. Wang, his wife, and four children live there, which is manageable. However, Mr. Wang's family has very few stools. Counting them, there's only one and a half. What does this mean? It turns out that besides the stool Mr. Wang sits on to write, there's only a broken long bench. The long bench originally had four legs, but now only two legs remain. No one knows who broke it. This long bench has changed from four legs to two legs, so you can only say it's half a stool. Therefore, Mr. Wang's family only has one and a half stools.

(3) All-Encompassing

Although Mr. Wang's family has few stools, they have many other things: there are two beds in total, and two tables as well. Other items like a stove, kerosene lamp, oil bottle, teacups, teapot, etc., are too numerous to count. Therefore, Mr. Wang's room is truly all-encompassing. There are beds where they sleep, which can be called the bedroom; there's a cupboard for bowls and chopsticks, where they eat, which can be called the dining room; Mr. Wang sits on the only complete stool to write, read newspapers, and study, which can be called the study; they also cook there, which is the kitchen; in the summer, they also bathe there, which is the bathroom; behind one of the beds, there's a chamber pot, which is the toilet. Mr. Wang's one-room home includes a bedroom, dining room, study, kitchen, bathroom, and toilet, truly deserving the description of all-encompassing.

New Philosophy 278

— Kefu

Midnight. The clock had struck one. My brother returned from a colleague's wedding, wearing two fresh and vibrant flowers.

"Is the bride pretty?" I asked, waking up and looking at him.

"Of course, the bride is a modern girl. She's a female teacher in her twenties. My colleague. Her wedding dress was rented from XX Company for 170 yuan!"

"I heard that the bride's dowry of 3,000 yuan was considered too little, and she refused to marry. They added another 1,000 yuan before she got into the sedan chair."

"Yes! She's been a primary school teacher for three years, with a head full of modern ideas. She's naturally read the philosophy of the 20th century thoroughly. Guess what kind of person her husband is?"

"A college graduate, a young man in a Western suit?"

"Your ideal philosophies are outdated! Who wouldn't think her husband is the young master of a soy sauce shop, an old-fashioned fellow in his thirties, with a face full of fat, thick eyebrows and big eyes, wearing a long gown, and with a full wallet."

"Oh! Why didn't she marry someone more handsome?"

"Ah, brother!" My brother took off his coat, somewhat excitedly, and said, "This is the true philosophy of the 20th century. It can be said that this lady's vision is not bad at all: what else is there to fear besides money?"

"Ah! Truly not bad! Only money won't fail!"

"Brother! Look at these two beautiful flowers I'm wearing!"

"Just bought with money, that's all!"

"·····················"

Night of the 9th,

Employee Communications

The Teller's Grievance 279

— Li Youzhang

Editor Sir:

Since I entered a certain store in this port in the year 18 of the Republic of China, I became acquainted with a colleague, Mr. So-and-so, and we became sworn brothers. In the year 20 of the Republic of China, I was promoted to teller. In the summer of the year 21, this sworn brother took leave to return to his hometown due to the passing of his father. At that time, he privately borrowed 25 silver dollars from me. Unexpectedly, before he returned to the store, I also suffered misfortune at home and had to return to my hometown. As usual, I handed over all the matters under my charge to another colleague designated by the manager. The matter of Mr. So-and-so's private borrowing was, of course, known to the manager, but he did not express any opinion. Two weeks later, my sworn brother returned to the store to work; I, due to various reasons, resigned and took another job. I recently received a letter from a former colleague informing me that Mr. So-and-so absconded with the funds last year; all the debts I handled have been ordered by the manager to be debited to my account; and a letter will be sent soon demanding repayment. I would like to ask whether I should acknowledge this debt; what harm acknowledging it would do to my reputation; and if I ignore it, can the manager guarantee to seek repayment from my guarantor? Furthermore, if this debt must be paid, can I entrust someone to transfer it? I eagerly await your reply. (The rest omitted)

Sincerely, Li Youzhang

XXXX

Editor's note: Money is truly a terrible thing; unless you escape from the world, you can be completely disconnected from it; otherwise, you will inevitably have to deal with it; and once you handle it, if you don't do it well, you will have to bear considerable responsibility. At that time, responsibility lies where it belongs, and you can't help but reluctantly acknowledge it.

Mr. Li's case is an example. Because Mr. Li wanted to eat, and wanted to eat more comfortably, when the manager promoted him to teller, he was naturally willing to accept, and he would definitely be very happy. But after becoming a teller, the trouble came: when his sworn brother discussed privately borrowing these twenty-five dollars, how could he refuse? Some people say that Mr. Li should not have failed to inform the manager and made his own decision at that time: but we think these platitudes are wrong. Think about how hard-hearted capitalists are: if he had reported it to the manager, this matter would have been hopeless: with the close brotherhood of Mr. Li, how could he harden his heart? Later, Mr. Li's sworn brother actually absconded with the funds; in the eyes of most people, they will blame Mr. Li again, saying, "Your judgment is too poor, you are so close to this good-for-nothing person, now you are suffering losses, it is truly pitiful and not worth pitying." We think this is wrong again; before a bad person is discovered, it is really not easy to distinguish them; moreover, most people who abscond with funds are forced by circumstances; unless they are extremely desperate.

Page 22

Who would be willing to do such a self-defeating thing? So, in our view, it is inevitable that Mr. Li feels unwilling to compensate for this money. But alas, this world is still under the monopoly of capitalism, and the law is also helping the capitalists; no matter how unwilling you are, you cannot escape responsibility. Even if you don't compensate, your guarantor will have to bear joint liability. As for the matter of whether acknowledging this debt will harm your reputation, this is not a problem; when you took leave to return to your hometown, the manager knew about this private borrowing, and his lack of objection was his acknowledgment that this money was indeed borrowed by your sworn brother. Now that you reluctantly compensate, it will not only not harm your reputation, but it will also show that you can take responsibility. Speaking of the method of delivery, it is of course best to deliver it in person, otherwise, entrusting someone to transfer it is also acceptable, but be careful not to entrust the wrong person again.

The Housing of Shanghai People 280

A Novel

Meishan (Continued) 281

— Written by EoFalkowski, translated by Zhixiang

Six

From the buildings on Jading and Ak Street, the workers who were sweating and whose lives were dictated by the mine whistles looked out. Every morning, the whistle drove them into the mysterious coal pits, and they didn't escape until evening. Their faces were covered in mud, and they wore foul-smelling clothes, suggesting the horrors of their lives in the coal pits, a place where ordinary people with leisurely lives could not imagine or stay long.

Miners couldn't imagine the joy of city dwellers. When the mine whistle blew, it easily revealed the differences in people's lives in society: one group of people, even though the whistle blew at six in the morning, could not be commanded by it and could still sleep soundly; another group of people, at this time, had to obey the whistle's command and run to the terrifying coal pit to struggle for bread.

This city was safely embraced in a mountain valley, undisturbed by the outside world. Many cities far away from here, such as New York and Boston, often had struggles over economics, but this small town embraced in the valley was very peaceful; only the smoke from the chimneys curled leisurely in the autumn dusk.

This city, like the smile of a sleepwalker, had passed year after year, with countless coal cars being transported to the market to compete with other fuels. Because of the recent strike, however, the sales of soft coal and kerosene exceeded those of hard coal, which had always been popular. It had occupied a superior position in the market in the past, but now it could no longer maintain it. The large advertisements in the newspapers confused the general public's eyes when buying fuel. At this time, the stoves seemed to show a cold and mocking look towards hard coal. Soft coal, whose sales had not been able to match hard coal in the past, was now greatly active in the basements that had previously only been the domain of expensive hard coal.

In the miners' union, based on the slogan of "cooperation and effectiveness," sympathy should have been shown to the workers on strike in the hard coal mines. Within the same union, the union leaders divided the common interests between the hard coal workers and the soft coal workers, drawing a line of demarcation. When the hard coal workers went on strike, the soft coal workers should have worked doubly hard to supply the fuel needs of society. Similarly, when the soft coal workers demanded better treatment and went on strike, the hard coal workers felt indifferent, and besides donating a small amount of money, they still worked as usual and happily worked hard to meet the urgent need for fuel. The union cleverly exploited this mutual indifference. Each practiced its own secrets, and this phenomenon continued.
